Con: The security provided by Israeli forces in the West Bank allows for [foreign investment](http://www.aipac.org/-/media/publications/policy-and-politics/aipac-analyses/issue-memos/2009/10/aipac_memo_israeli_measures_in_west_bank_easing_palestinian_travel_boosting_economy.ashx) to pour into the area.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1. Con: It is likely that even more foreign investment would have poured into the Palestinian territories if it were not for Israeli policies that stifle the Palestinian economy, as well as the repeated invasions of Gaza.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.3.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2. Pro: The continued blockade [prevents economic development](http://www.btselem.org/gaza-strip/gaza-strip-siege-gaza-and-intensified-economic-sanctions) of Gaza, forcing economic dependence on Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2.1. Pro: Gazans are, on average, [worse off than in the 1990s](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-20415675). Twenty-one percent are in deep poverty, living on less than 1,832 shekels \($534; £313\) a month, compared with 7.8% in the West Bank. The unemployment rate in the Strip is 40.8%, significantly higher than in the West Bank. Of particular concern is the high youth unemployment rate, which stands at more than 50% in Gaza.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2.2. Pro: The Israeli blockade of Gaza [hampers](http://www.un.org/apps/news/story.asp?NewsID=30948#.WPapC1KZORt) UN relief work. Important construction material required for rebuilding houses and roads is not allowed to enter Gaza.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2.3. Con: Israel [continues](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-s-quot-blockade-quot-of-gaza) to supply electricity and water to the Palestinian people, and these plants are sometimes hit by rockets fired by Hamas from within the Gaza Strip, cutting power to thousands.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2.3.1. Con: Yet Gaza's only power plant was [destroyed](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/jul/29/gaza-power-plant-destroyed-israeli-airstrike-100-palestinians-dead) in one of Israel's most intense air strikes in the occupied territory.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.3. Pro: Israel has repeatedly undertaken military operations to stem the tide of Palestinian terrorism. This can be seen in [Operation Defensive Shield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Defensive_Shield) in 2002, the 2008/9 [invasion of Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_\(2008–09\)), and [Operation Pillar of Defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Pillar_of_Defense) in 2012.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.7. Con: Israeli [security forces](http://www.aipac.org/-/media/publications/policy-and-politics/aipac-analyses/issue-memos/2009/10/aipac_memo_israeli_measures_in_west_bank_easing_palestinian_travel_boosting_economy.ashx) are training their Palestinian peers to be more effective in fighting terror in Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8. Pro: Palestinian opportunities for education are limited because of the occupation.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.1. Pro: Israel's decision to withhold taxes from the Palestinian Authority causes a severe lack of funding for schools \([Roberston, p. 33](https://download.ei-ie.org/Docs/WebDepot/The%20Status%20of%20Higher%20Education%20Teaching%20Personnel%20in%20Israel,%20the%20West%20Bank%20and%20Gaza.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.2. Con: There are more universities now than [before](https://unitedwithisrael.org/the-facts-show-israeli-occupation-is-good-for-the-palestinians/) the West Bank occupation
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.2.1. Con: The UN and not Israel is providing the bulk of education in the West Bank and Gaza \([UNDP, p. 3](http://www.ps.undp.org/content/dam/papp/docs/Publications/UNDP-papp-research-PHDR2015Education.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.2.2. Con: The Palestine Technical-Tulkarem University College and the Al-Ummah Community College were established before 1967 \([Robinson, p. 32](https://download.ei-ie.org/Docs/WebDepot/The%20Status%20of%20Higher%20Education%20Teaching%20Personnel%20in%20Israel,%20the%20West%20Bank%20and%20Gaza.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.2.3. Pro: In the period of the British Mandate, the Peel Commission identified the lack of higher education opportunities for Palestinians as a major source of concern \([Robinson, p. 31](https://download.ei-ie.org/Docs/WebDepot/The%20Status%20of%20Higher%20Education%20Teaching%20Personnel%20in%20Israel,%20the%20West%20Bank%20and%20Gaza.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.8.2.4. Con: The number of universities in Palestine is not a good indicator of what Israel has done. These universities could have been created in spite of Israel, rather than because of Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.4. Con: Though a coordinated withdrawal is theoretically possible, it may be difficult to achieve. Israeli unwillingness to withdraw could mean that efforts to adequately coordinate withdrawal fails.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.2. Con: The Israeli/Egyptian blockade only applies to the Gaza Strip. The West Bank is able to trade with much fewer exceptions, thus trade negotiations are still important.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3. Pro: This could provoke Israel to act aggressively against Palestine in reaction, which could result in worsened conditions for Palestinians.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.1. Con: Israel has fought at least 3 wars in Palestine in the last decade and regularly conducts air and artillery strikes against Gaza. It is difficult to see how they could act more aggressively.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2. Con: If the United States were to recognize Palestine, it is unlikely that Israel would position itself against not only the majority of the international community but also its most important ally by becoming more aggressive towards Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1. Pro: Israel is far too [dependent](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential) on aid from the US to destroy relations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.1. Pro: Israel's trade is [highly dependent](http://atlas.media.mit.edu/en/profile/country/isr/#Destinations) on the United States: 37% of its exports go to America, 14% of its imports come from there. No other country plays an equivalent role for Israel's trade.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.1.1. Pro: In fact, Israel exports [more](http://atlas.media.mit.edu/en/visualize/tree_map/hs92/export/isr/show/all/2015/) to the United States than to its eleven next largest trade partners combined.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.2. Pro: No other country sends as many tourists to Israel as the United States. American tourists make up almost [one quarter](http://www.cbs.gov.il/publications17/yarhon0317/pdf/e7.pdf) of all tourism arrivals in Israel - and American tourists have in the past [shunned](http://www.cbsnews.com/news/us-tourism-to-france-perks-up/) countries they perceived to act in opposition to US interests.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.2.1. Con: Because of the religious and cultural importance of Israel to both Christians and Jews, the two largest religious groups in the U.S., many Americans will have reasons to visit Israel independent of U.S. official policies.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3. Pro: The US supports Israel diplomatically.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.1. Pro: The US has repeatedly voted against all other members of the UN Security Council, vetoing resolutions that would have criticized Israel. For example, resolutions on [settlement](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/F97C162F6A30647205256531005B4E15) [expansions](http://www.securitycouncilreport.org/un-documents/document/IP%20S2011%2024.php), [assassinations](http://www.securitycouncilreport.org/un-documents/document/IP%202004%20240.php), violating the [Geneva Convention](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/5ba47a5c6cef541b802563e000493b8c/b35c281bef2fa8f00525651b003675d3?OpenDocument) and [attacking UN supplies and killing UN workers](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/87CD207B928B40D885256C950067EF41).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.2. Pro: The United States has adopted a "[don't ask, don't tell](http://www.80bola.com.nuclearfiles.org/menu/key-issues/nuclear-weapons/issues/proliferation/israel/Israel%20crosses%20the%20threshold.pdf)" attitude towards Israel's nuclear program - a privilege which no other officially non-nuclear state enjoys.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.3. Con: American diplomatic support for Israel has [never been unequivocal](https://sethfrantzman.com/2016/12/24/abstaining-from-history-heres-all-the-un-resolutions-on-israel-the-us-abstained-on/). The US has supported, abstained from and vetoed UN resolutions criticizing Israel in the past.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.3.1. Con: Until December 2016, out of 226 UN Security Council resolutions related to Israel since 1948, the US has [abstained](https://sethfrantzman.com/2016/12/24/abstaining-from-history-heres-all-the-un-resolutions-on-israel-the-us-abstained-on/) from less than two dozen of them. It has only voted against Israel a handful of times.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.4. Pro: Even when the US was supposed to play a neutral role - for example during the negotiations of the Oslo Accords in 1993 and in Camp David in 2000 - it de-facto [sided with Israel](https://www.lrb.co.uk/v28/n06/john-mearsheimer/the-israel-lobby).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4. Con: [Israel's status as a nuclear power](http://www.rense.com/general26/historw.htm) allows the country to be independent of the whims of major powers like the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.1. Con: Hamas and Hezbollah are the main threats faced by Israel, both of which are terrorist organisations. Nuclear weapons are effective deterrence against states, not non-state actors. Therefore, Israel's nuclear weapons do not grant it total independence.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.2. Con: Without tacit American acquiescence, the international community might call into question Israel's nuclear program and attempt to pressure the country into signing the Nuclear Non Proliferation Treaty.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.3.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.2.2. Pro: There has been [international pressure](http://www.jpost.com/Middle-East/Israel-Under-Pressure-To-Give-Up-Chemical-Nuclear-Weapons-326452) on Israel to give up its nuclear weapons - without the support of the US, this international pressure may increase and force Israel to give up its nuclear weapons.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.2.3. Con: The outsized [power](http://www.yourarticlelibrary.com/international-politics/impact-of-nuclear-weapons-on-international-relations/48526/) that any nuclear power has in international relations would likely continue to insulate Israel from any pressures to end their nuclear weapons program.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5. Con: Israel has a [large conventional arms industry](http://www.spiegel.de/international/world/defense-industry-the-business-of-war-in-israel-a-988245.html). As a result, Israel's security is not dependent on good relations with the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.1. Pro: Israel's defense industry is actually [undermined by US aid](http://forward.com/news/breaking-news/350424/israel-arms-industry-sees-big-hit-from-buy-american-provisions-in-38b-aid-d/) which forces it to "buy American". By restricting the amount that can be spent domestically, Israel's defence industry faces layoffs and closures.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2. Con: Although Israel produces advanced battle tanks and drones, it is by no means self-sufficient in terms of equipping its armed forces. For airplanes, to name but one example, it is wholly dependent on procurement from the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2.1. Pro: All airplanes and nearly all helicopters of the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force#Aircraft) were bought from the US. With an eye on its international position, it is unlikely that Israel would be able to procure military technology on this level from elsewhere.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2.1.1. Con: Dependence on US aid has [institutionalized](https://townhall.com/columnists/jeffjacoby/2016/09/05/israel-doesnt-need-american-foreign-aid-n2213875) Israeli reliance on air power and ever-more-advanced technology, at the expense of focusing more intensively on ground maneuvers and the unique threat posed by enemies waging asymmetric warfare. Israel would be better off without this aid.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2.1.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6. Pro: Israel receives almost 1% of its GDP in foreign aid from the United States, more than any other country and about 9% of America's foreign assistance budget \([State Department, p. 16, 20](https://www.state.gov/documents/organization/224071.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.1. Con: Israel's dependency is shrinking. Whereas the size of its economy [has tripled](http://data.worldbank.org/country/israel) over the last two decades, the size of aid payments has stayed the same. The share of US aid among Israel's GDP thus sunk from about 3% to 1% \([CRS, p. 23](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33476.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.2. Pro: US aid accounts for [20% of Israel's defence budget and 40% of the IDF budget](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential). Israel is therefore heavily dependent on the US to maintain its defences.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.2.1. Con: Israel can hardly be said to be militarily dependent on the US. Even excluding America's military aid, it spends [one and a half times](https://www.sipri.org/databases/milex) as much on its military than all of its neighbors combined; the share of its GDP that it spends on the military is [the highest](https://www.sipri.org/sites/default/files/Trends-world-military-expenditure-2016.pdf) among all the world's major armies.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.2.3. Pro: The US also provides [vital defense technologies](http://www.belfercenter.org/publication/israels-dependence-united-states-existential) that Israel would not have access to otherwise.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.3. Pro: U.S. military aid for Israel has been designed to maintain Israel’s “[qualitative military edge](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)” \(QME\) \(pg. 1\) over neighbouring militaries. This is vital to its regional security.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.3.1. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.4.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.7. Con: It would be politically unviable for the US to completely cut off its aid to Israel, as [most US voters](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) are staunchly pro-Israel \(or would at least oppose the US substantially cutting off aid\) so Israel still has plenty of room to become more intransigent and aggressive in reaction to this sort of move.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.7.1. Con: Israel could be made to feel its dependence on the United States even without a complete cut-off of relations. In 2004, the American government already [threatened to](http://www.meforum.org/926/at-what-cost-israel-china-ties) exclude Israel from the F-35 jet program - and thus Israel's primary way of updating its air force.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.7.2. Con: [46%](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of Americans support imposing sanctions on Israel in response to settlement-building.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.7.3. Pro: American citizens' views of Israel have remained steadily positive since [2001](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx), despite occasional Israel aggression against Palestine. While many might think some sanctions are acceptable, cutting off aid completely would likely be a step too far in the eyes of pro-Israel Americans.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.2. Con: Israel tends to [respond harshly](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/un-security-council-vote-resolution-settlements-west-bank-east-jerusalem-israel-netanyahu-a7493996.html) when the international community moves against it. It did so when the UN condemned Israeli settlements: Israel withdrew its ambassadors from countries that voted in favour of the resolution and refused to follow the resolution.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.3. Con: Israel is already largely isolated in international public opinion but - so far - did not see this as a reason to change its policies.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.3.1. Pro: Israel has few other allies and is generally not seen favourably abroad. In the [BBC's popularity ranking](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-22624104), it is on one of the last ranks, just ahead of North Korea.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.3.2. Pro: Surveys from countries like Britain show Israel's unpopularity. Among non-European countries, British people feel more unfavorable only towards North Korea; even Iran is perceived as more favorable than Israel \([Chatham House, p. 11](https://www.chathamhouse.org/sites/files/chathamhouse/field/field_document/20150129YouGovRaines.pdf?dm_i=1TY5,34ZC7,BHZIRQ,B8VH2,1)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3. Con: Palestine does not pose a [military threat](https://imeu.org/article/comparison-of-millitary-strength-of-israel-and-the-palestinians) to Israel, so the need for aggressive action is minimal, if not non-existent.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.1. Con: While Palestine does not possess the military capacity to destroy Israel, the threat of terrorist attacks and mortar fire from groups such as Hamas still exists.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.1.1. Pro: [Every year](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/comprehensive-listing-of-terrorism-victims-in-israel) Israelis die from terror attacks committed by Palestinians or launched from Palestinian territory.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.1.2. Pro: As of May 2016, two thirds of Israeli citizens were afraid that they or someone close to them might be hurt by a terror attack \([IDI, p. 5](http://www.peaceindex.org/files/Peace_Index_Data_April_2016-Eng\(1\).pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.2. Con: Though Palestine may not currently pose a military threat to Israel, they still [consider](http://www.mintpressnews.com/palestinian-statehood-poses-threat-israel/200249/) Palestine to be an inherent threat to their own existence. Because Israel fears Palestine, they could feel it vital to strike against Palestine before they become strong enough to pose an actual military threat.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4. Pro: Recognition would constitute a big step towards increasing Palestine's chances to become an independent state. Israel does not want this to happen and would want to prevent this while it's still possible.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.2.1.2.1.3.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.2. Pro: Part of the reason Netanyahu won [re-election](https://www.voanews.com/a/how-netanyahu-pulled-off-israeli-election-win/2685053.html) was because of his strong anti-Palestine rhetoric. A claim that US recognition of Palestine means that they become a larger threat, followed by harsher actions against Palestine, would gain him more support from his voter-base.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.2.1. Pro: The [rally-round-the-flag](http://www.jstor.org.proxy.mah.se/stable/3649343?Search=yes&resultItemClick=true&searchText=anatomy&searchText=of&searchText=a&searchText=rally&searchText=effect:&searchText=George&searchText=W&searchText=Bush&searchUri=%2Faction%2FdoBasicSearch%3Fwc%3Don%26amp%3Bacc%3Don%26amp%3Bprq%3Danatomy%2Bof%2Bthe%2Brally%2Beffect%26amp%3Bfc%3Doff%26amp%3BQuery%3Danatomy%2Bof%2Ba%2Brally%2Beffect%253A%2BGeorge%2BW%2BBush%26amp%3Bso%3Drel%26amp%3Bhp%3D25&refreqid=search%3Af88037627ed90e32fb48fe293779dc21&seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) effect is a sudden increase in approval ratings following periods of international crisis or war. The effect is mainly in reference to [US presidents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rally_%27round_the_flag_effect) but Netanyahu could benefit from the same effect among his more patriotic supporters, should he attack Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.2.2. Pro: Netanyahu is currently under an [investigation](http://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-gifts-investigation-to-drag-on-until-autumn-report/) for corruption that could drag on for several more months. Acting aggressive in response to a US recognition of Palestine would serve as an effective distraction from this scandal.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.3. Pro: Recognition of Palestine has prompted retaliation from Israel in the past.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.3.1. Pro: Israel suspended a payment of [$127 million](https://www.amnestyusa.org/press-releases/retaliation-against-palestines-welcome-accession-to-icc-must-stop/) due to the Palestinian authorities, as a response to Palestine's accession to the ICC a day after the statute was signed.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.3.2. Pro: In response to the UN's recognition of Palestine, Israel confiscated [£75 million](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/middleeast/israel/9717397/Israel-exacts-retaliation-for-Palestinian-statehood-vote-as-it-confiscates-75m-in-revenue.html) that it was supposed to pay Palestine and announced that it would build 3000 new settlers' home in areas that the Palestinians had earmarked as part of a future state.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4. Pro: In order to prevent Palestine from being empowered by US recognition, Israel would likely increase the amount of harm that they already inflict upon Palestinians.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.1. Pro: Israeli settlements harm Palestinians.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.1.1. Pro: In the West Bank, water resources have been [seized](http://www.alhaq.org/publications/Water-For-One-People-Only.pdf) \(p. 16\) such that the Israeli settler population, numbering more than 500,000, consumes approximately six times the amount of water used by the Palestinian population of almost 2.6 million; this discrepancy is even greater when water used for agricultural purposes is taken into account.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.3.6.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.3.6.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.1.4. Pro: Palestinian labourers who work in these settlements are [exploited](https://www.btselem.org/download/201105_dispossession_and_exploitation_eng.pdf) \(p. 37\). They are paid as little as one-third the minimum wage they are entitled to receive, with the employers consistently violating safety regulations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.4.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.4.3.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.2.1.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.6. Con: Even if the situation of Palestinians did not improve, this would be blamed on Israeli intransigence, and the US would no longer share a significant portion of the blame.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.2. Pro: Since recognition of Palestine would mean diplomatic relations with the US and potentially full membership in the UN, it is likely that less people would be motivated to join Hamas as they would feel less oppressed.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2. Con: While the specific combination of psychological factors that cause an individual to become a terrorist may be unpredictable, scholars can identify [patterns](http://www.jstor.org.tkc.idm.oclc.org/stable/421717) among the types of causes which recruit terrorists \(and the [Palestinian conflict](http://hegghammer.com/_files/The_Palestine_Effect_The_Role_of_Palestinians_in_the_Transnational_Jihad_Movement.pdf) is one such cause\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2.1. Pro: When Americans conduct an illegal [drone strike](http://chrgj.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/Living-Under-Drones.pdf) in the Middle East or Israel kills Palestinian [civilians](http://thehill.com/policy/international/214255-dem-senator-civilian-deaths-a-recruitment-tool-for-hamas), recruiting for terrorist organizations increases, demonstrating a causal relationship between certain conflicts and terrorism.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2.1.1. Con: Invasive and aggressive American foreign policy will continue regardless of how the US treats the Palestinian issue.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2.2. Pro: [News coverage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_12,_2007_Baghdad_airstrike) of massacres or collateral murder, such as the Baghdad airstrikes in 2007, antagonizes bystanders and supports radical thinking against the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.5.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.5. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4. Con: The terrorist organisations who have declared war on the US would continue to fight against it independent of the situation in Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4.1. Pro: The [US war in Iraq](http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=6137678) has significantly increased the threat of terrorism. This is independent of the Palestinian issue.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4.2. Pro: ISIS wants to establish a [global caliphate](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2015/03/what-isis-really-wants/384980/), which is also the long term goal of [al-Qaeda](http://www.spiegel.de/international/the-future-of-terrorism-what-al-qaida-really-wants-a-369448.html). This goal will remain regardless of how friendly the US will be to Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4.3. Pro: Certain [interpretations](http://www.thereligionofpeace.com/quran/023-violence.htm) of Islam encourage killing non-Muslims. These interpretations exists regardless of US actions.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2.1.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.4.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.5.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5. Con: It is unlikely that Palestinian organizations commit acts of terror in the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.1. Pro: As of now, Hamas has not targeted US citizens \([Benjamin & Simon, p. 194](https://books.google.de/books?id=IOoBZvdNrIkC&printsec=frontcover&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q=%22Thus%20far%2C%20Hamas%22&f=false)\), proving that their threats are little more than non-serious rhetoric.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.2. Con: Just because Palestinian organisations do not commit terror acts in the US does not mean that the Palestinian cause does not inspire other terrorist groups.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.3. Con: ISIS-linked groups have a presence both [in Gaza](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/hamas-fighters-defect-isis-islamic-state-nukhba-commando-iz-ad-din-al-qassam-gaza-palestinian-group-a7569786.html) and [the West Bank](http://www.jpost.com/Arab-Israeli-Conflict/3-ISIS-inspired-Arab-Israelis-plotted-tunnel-from-West-Bank-into-Israel-470036). This organisation has already [attempted](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/02/04/world/asia/isis-messaging-app-terror-plot.html) significant terror attacks on US soils.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4. Pro: There is little to no evidence that international terrorist organisations willing and capable of striking the US, like al-Quaeda, are linked to Palestinian groups \([Mearsheimer & Walt, p. 63](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=bQHXJ4JzxV4C&pg=PT3&lpg=PT3&dq=0-374-17772-4&source=bl&ots=APimckevjw&sig=iq9yYeg467Yc6VnXh-YNhuozdSA&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjG7tjIobfUAhWCgbwKHeWAAcUQ6AEIJjAB#v=onepage&q=0-374-17772-4&f=false)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.1. Con: [Ma’sadat al-Mujahideen](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/middle-east/israel-fires-haifa-jerusalem-terror-palestinian-militant-group-ma-sadat-al-mujahideen-mount-carmel-a7439271.html) is an al-Qaeda linked Palestinian Salafist group. It has claimed to be behind several fires in Israel, including the Mount Carmel forest fire that killed more than 40 people near Haifa in 2010 and the 2016 Haifa blaze that led to the evacuation of 60,000 people.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.2. Con: [Army of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Islam_\(Gaza_Strip\)) is a militant group that operates in the Gaza Strip. It draws inspiration from and is likely linked to al-Qaeda.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.3. Con: Hamas has [loose ties](http://www.weeklystandard.com/the-hamas-al-qaeda-alliance/article/558605) with al-Qaeda: Hamas members receive training from al-Qaeda camps and often try to recruit fighters for their cause from al-Qaeda as well.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.4. Con: Al-Qaeda has a [history](http://www.jpost.com/Opinion/Op-Ed-Contributors/Al-Qaida-and-Palestinian-jihadists-The-Hamas-connection-339782) of conducting attacks in Israel by recruiting and sending in foreign fighters. After al-Qaeda started losing ground in Afghanistan, bin Laden marked Palestine as a top priority. Al-Qaeda does not need to be linked to Palestinian organisations in order to operate within Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.4.1. Pro: The shoe bomber, Richard Reid, trained by Al-Qaeda in Afghanistan, traveled to Israel in 2001 to [scout out](http://content.time.com/time/world/article/0,8599,203478-1,00.html) locations for potential bombings.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.4.2. Con: There is little to no evidence connecting the central leadership of Al-Qaeda with attacks in Israel or on other Jewish targets. These attacks therefore do not adequately reflect the importance designated to Israel by Al-Qaeda \([Hegghammer/Wagemakers, p. 291](http://hegghammer.com/_files/The_Palestine_Effect_The_Role_of_Palestinians_in_the_Transnational_Jihad_Movement.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.5. Pro: Al-Qaeda has [consistently](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/the-war-of-words-between-hamas-and-al-qaeda) condemned the Hamas leadership whenever they have run for elections or tried to work with Fatah in a unity government; Al-Qaeda's support for Hamas exists only when the latter adopts a military approach to the Palestinian conflict.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.6. Pro: Hamas - Al-Qaeda interactions were negligible during the 1990's and 2000's \([T. Hegghammer and co., p. 285](http://hegghammer.com/_files/The_Palestine_Effect_The_Role_of_Palestinians_in_the_Transnational_Jihad_Movement.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.5.4.7. Pro: Despite threatening to, Hamas has not joined Al-Qaeda's global jihad. Hamas sees itself as a [local resistance organization](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/policy-analysis/view/could-hamas-target-the-west) and has limited its operations to targeting Israelis in Israel, the West Bank, and the Gaza Strip.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2. Pro: Recognition will lead to an improved image of the US in the Arab world.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1. Con: Any improvement of America's reputation in the region will be limited as the Israel-Palestine question is only one of many issues that determine how America is seen.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.1. Pro: Negative [stereotypes](http://www.pewglobal.org/2011/07/21/chapter-2-how-muslims-and-westerners-view-each-other/) about Westerners as 'selfish', 'violent' or 'greedy' help to perpetuate Anti-Americanism.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.2. Con: Surveys have found that the Palestinian question is a significant determinant of attitudes towards America.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.2.1. Pro: In the Arab World, the Palestinian question is a [significant](http://www.pewresearch.org/2005/11/10/arab-and-muslim-perceptions-of-the-united-states/) determinant of attitudes towards America.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.3. Pro: The US supports corrupt autocracies in the region and thus [fuels](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/steve-koppman/endless-us-support-for-di_b_6821136.html) anti-Americanism \([Lindberg & Nossel, p. 9](https://www.princeton.edu/~ppns/conferences/reports/fall/AA.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.3.1. Pro: In non-democratic countries supported by and allied with the US, such as Iraq, the United Arab Emirates and Jordan, the lack of representative government is seen as the primary obstacle to peace and stability in the region \([Zogby, p. 11](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4. Pro: The US has a track record of military interventions in the Middle East which have negatively shaped perceptions.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.1. Pro: The presence of US soldiers alienates the local population.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.1.1. Pro: The [habits](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/saudi-arabia-withdrawl-us-forces) of US soldiers radicalize some locals as they drink alcohol and behave outside social norms, as was observed in Saudi Arabia.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.1.2. Pro: US military bases and soldiers are a magnet for [terrorist attacks](https://www.cfr.org/backgrounder/saudi-arabia-withdrawl-us-forces), risking the lives of those nearby. In the 1990s, the base in Saudi Arabia was moved because of this.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.2. Pro: A military presence is interpreted by some as an all out [war against Islam](https://theintercept.com/2016/10/11/us-military-operations-are-biggest-motivation-for-homegrown-terrorists-fbi-study-finds/). For individuals that link their identity to Islam, this can be seen as an attack on themselves.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.3. Pro: The violence and death caused as a result of these military interventions leads to resentment towards the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.2.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.4.3.2. Con: American interference in the region is generally not seen by public opinion as one of the most severe obstacles to peace and stability in the region - not even in countries directly affected by it like Iraq \([Zogby, p. 11](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.5. Con: Surveys show that American culture and political values are generally seen as positive, whereas American policies in the Middle East evoke opposition - with the policies towards Palestine being among the prime sources \([Chiozza, p. 15](http://politics.as.nyu.edu/docs/IO/4737/chiozza_f04.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.2. Pro: A favourable image of the US allows for a better relationship between the US and Arab countries to form, which could lead to better trade agreements and intelligence sharing.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.2.1. Con: If there are pragmatic benefits to be gained through cooperation, Middle Eastern states will cooperate with the US regardless of "perception" of the US' morality as an actor.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.2.2. Pro: The US conducts operations in several countries in the Middle East, which they could do more easily if Arab countries had a more positive image of the US. Willingness to help and cooperate would likely be higher if the attitude towards the US were more positive.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.2.2.1. Pro: In their operations in Iraq, the US military [relied heavily](https://www.pri.org/stories/2017-01-31/iraqi-translators-who-served-us-military-are-desperate-exemption-trumps-travel) on assistance from local translators. The willingness of translators to cooperate, and of the local population to tolerate people who cooperate with the US military, was dependent on public perception of the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.2.3. Con: Given that most Middle Eastern nations, including Saudi Arabia and Egypt, [aren't democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_Index), it does not matter what the populace believes as much as what the government believes is in its regional security and economic interests.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3. Pro: The Palestinian conflict colours public perception of the US in the Middle East.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.1. Pro: The people of major US allies such as Saudi Arabia and Egypt as well as of important regional players like Turkey see the occupation of Palestinian territories as the greatest threat to peace and stability in the region. America could gather sympathies by recognizing Palestine \([Zogby, p. 10](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.1.1. Con: Egypt's relations with Israel are the [best they have been in history](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2016/11/egypt-israel-relations-highest-level-history-161107083926863.html). They both cooperate on regional security concerns such as Hamas and terrorist groups in the Sinai peninsula, and Egypt's calls for peace between Israel and Palestinians are widely considered as empty rhetoric that is not accompanied by any diplomatic pressure on Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.1.2. Con: The same study states that the people in Iran, Jordan, Lebanon and Iraq give scant attention to the Palestinian issue \([Zogby, p. 10](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\)
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.1.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.3. Pro: A US government report found that attitudes by citizens of Egypt, Syria, Turkey, France, Morocco and Senegal are inspired by their concerns for Palestine \([Djerejian, p. 18](https://www.state.gov/documents/organization/24882.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4. Con: Given that most Middle Eastern nations, including Saudi Arabia and Egypt, [aren't democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_Index), it does not matter what the populace believes as much as what the government believes is in its regional security and economic interests.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4.1. Pro: Israel [opened](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/samuel-ramani/why-israel-is-strengthening_b_11946660.html) its first diplomatic mission in the United Arab Emirates \(UAE\) three months after it stopped bombing Gaza in 2015. The Gulf states have signed covert deals with the Israeli defence contractors to gain access to the IDF’s prized military technology. This is used to secure oil wells. Economic interests trump the demand for a Palestinian state.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4.2. Con: Even dictatorships are receptive to popular will to some extent. Complete disregard for popular opinion always leads to instability.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4.3. Con: The fact that these countries have backdoor relations with Israel indicates that these relations are important for their regional security and economic interests. Being able to establish a more open relationship is in their interests; these countries will therefore care about whether public opinion permits an open relationship.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4.3.1. Con: Pressuring Israel for a peace deal will likely alienate it as Israel does not want to recognise an independent Palestine. This risks destroying whatever gains have been made through backdoor and covert diplomacy.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.4.4. Con: While it might be that popular perception is not as important for state actors to the extent that they are non-democratic, it still influences many other aspects of national relations, since a nation is far more than simply its state.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.5. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.3.1.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4. Con: Any benefit to US/Arab relations would be negligible at best and at worst it would be seen as a betrayal of one of their key regional allies, Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.1. Pro: US allies in the Middle East are more concerned about their own socio-economic conditions and security than about Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.2. Pro: Israel's enemies around the world \(including Hamas and the PA\) will not be pacified by recognition, or even the creation of a Palestinian state - only by the destruction of the Jewish one.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.2.1. Pro: Hamas and other vocal enemies of Israel could hardly sell more amicable relations to their domestic audiences and supporters after decades of hateful rhetoric towards Israel and threats of destruction.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3. Con: America shouldn't be concerned about the reaction in Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.1. Pro: Israel does not behave as an ally to the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.1.1. Pro: Israel has consistently spied on the United States. [See the Jonathan Pollard trial.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Pollard)
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.1.2. Pro: The Israeli Prime Minister [went to the US congress](https://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-spat-in-our-face-white-house-officials-say/) to undermine the President of the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.1.3. Pro: Israel's [diplomatic efforts against the most important multilateral deal](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-israel/israels-netanyahu-draws-rebuke-from-obama-over-iran-speech-to-congress-idUSKBN0LZ0BS20150303) led by Obama were not consistent with an alliance.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.2. Pro: While one might expect one of America's closest allies to play a supportive role in times of conflict, Israel has been a strategic burden in the past, for example during the Gulf War in 1990 and 1991. The US government [intentionally had to keep](http://users.ox.ac.uk/~ssfc0005/Israel%20and%20the%20Conflict.html) Israel out of the coalition against Iraq. Its participation might have led to more Arab support for Iraq and possibly even Arab countries leaving the coalition.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.2.1. Con: This singular instance from a quarter of a century ago is hardly representative of the United States' relationship with Israel as a whole.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.5. Pro: All Arab countries [recognise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine) Palestine as a state.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.6. Pro: Given the US's long history of [intense opposition](http://edition.cnn.com/2016/12/28/politics/ben-rhodes-veto-un-resolution-palestinian-state-obama/) to the recognition of Palestinian statehood, a decision this unprecedented and of this magnitude would have a massive impact on the attitudes of Arab nations towards the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.6.1. Con: US recognition would be unlikely to actually alleviate the plight of the Palestinian people, so anger at the US for perpetuating the conflict up to the present day would persist.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7. Pro: As recognition of Palestine would be perceived as a step in opposition to Israel's stated interests, this is likely to be perceived positively throughout the Middle East.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7.1. Pro: Practically no one in major Middle Eastern countries has a positive opinion of Israel, sees the country as a contributor to peace and stability in the region, or perceives relations with Israel as important \([Zogby, p. 5, 7, 8](https://d3n8a8pro7vhmx.cloudfront.net/aai/pages/12021/attachments/original/1481751962/SBY2016_FINAL.pdf?1481751962)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7.1.1. Con: There exists a '[moderate axis](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20140723-israeli-general-the-moderate-axis-is-helping-us-fight-hamas/)' of [Middle Eastern nations](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2016/11/egypt-israel-relations-highest-level-history-161107083926863.html), including Egypt, Turkey, Saudi Arabia and several of the Gulf states, as well as Jordan, that have offered Israel a wide margin of flexibility to pursue the war on Hamas. Public calls for peace are accompanied by backdoor diplomacy.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7.1.1.1. Pro: These nations [perceive](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/07/31/world/middleeast/fighting-political-islam-arab-states-find-themselves-allied-with-israel.html?_r=0) Hamas to be an Islamist threat that could destabilise their own countries. Iran's support and funding of Hamas has effectively made these nations prioritise the destruction of the group over the recognition of a Palestinian state.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7.1.1.2. Pro: The Gulf states [fear](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/samuel-ramani/why-israel-is-strengthening_b_11946660.html) Hamas' link with the Muslim Brotherhood, which they believe is backed by Iran.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3. Con: This will alienate Israel and damage US-Israeli relations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1. Con: Even though the current Israeli government is not negotiating, the Israeli public [supports](http://www.inss.org.il/uploadImages/systemFiles/No.%20916%20-%20Israeli%20on%20National%20Security%20Index.pdf) the establishment of a Palestinian state - [even if](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) safeguards need to be established \(e.g. a multinational security force\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.1. Con: At the same time, only about [a third of Israelis](http://www.pcpsr.org/en/node/678) support the idea of splitting control over Jerusalem. This indicates that, although most Israelis are committed to a two-state solution in principle, in practice they are unwilling to make the concessions necessary to achieve such a solution.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2. Con: While the Israeli public may not oppose the creation of a Palestinian state, the political establishment does, and the political establishment decides what Israel's official stance on the creation of a Palestinian state is.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2.1. Pro: Right wing Israeli politicians, after the election of Donald Trump, have [declared](http://www.jpost.com/US-Elections/Donald-Trump/Likud-MKs-react-to-Trumps-victory-in-US-Presidential-Election-472088) the era of a Palestinian state as over.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2.1.1. Pro: Naftali Bennett, leader of the Jewish Home party - a lynchpin of Israel’s nationalist right and current coalition partner and Education Minister - stated that there will [never](http://www.timesofisrael.com/bennett-no-palestinian-state-even-if-world-penalizes-israel/) be a Palestinian state, even if the world penalises Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.2.1.2.1.3.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2.3. Con: If the public supports a two-state solution, then if the political establishment maintains its opposition to the idea, it will likely be voted out in future elections.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.2.3.1. Con: Only [16%](http://www.timesofisrael.com/for-43-of-likely-voters-economic-issues-not-the-palestinians-or-iran-are-top-priority/) of Israeli voters ranked deterioration of relations with Palestinians as their most important issue in the 2013 elections. The two-state solution will likely not be the deciding factor in any election.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.1.3. Pro: Surveys emphasize that the support for a two-state solution would probably be at more than 70% in case of a referendum, as about a quarter of the population usually states that they are undecided or unsure \([INSS, p. 2](http://www.inss.org.il/uploadImages/systemFiles/No.%20916%20-%20Israeli%20on%20National%20Security%20Index.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2. Con: Surveys indicate that the American public would be in support of less amicable and supportive relations with Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.1. Pro: [More than half](http://www.washingtonreport.me/2017-may/grant-smith-american-public-opinion-about-u.s.-aid-to-israel-and-other-top-aipac-programs.html) of Americans believe that their government should abandon the principle of not openly criticizing Israel and its policies, as some demand.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.2. Pro: [Six out of ten](http://www.washingtonreport.me/2017-may/grant-smith-american-public-opinion-about-u.s.-aid-to-israel-and-other-top-aipac-programs.html) Americans believe that the United States gives too much or even far too much foreign aid to Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.3. Con: However, less amicable and supportive relations are not the same thing as unilaterally recognising Palestine at the expense of American-Israeli relations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.4. Pro: [The vast majority](http://www.washingtonreport.me/2017-may/grant-smith-american-public-opinion-about-u.s.-aid-to-israel-and-other-top-aipac-programs.html) of Americans oppose the system by which campaign contributions are paid to members of Congress based on their stance towards Israel. This indicates that Americans are unhappy with the extent to which Congress is assumed by default to support Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.4.1. Con: This indicates unhappiness towards politicians supporting Israel by default, not against supporting Israel for rational reasons. The former is a corruption of democracy, while the latter is a politician doing their job.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.3. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4. Pro: This will likely alienate Israel further from any negotiations towards a two-state solution.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.2. Pro: The right wing establishment in Israel is thoroughly [opposed](https://www.i24news.tv/en/news/israel/diplomacy-defense/137396-170211-minister-says-israel-faces-historic-opportunity-to-nix-two-state-solution) to the creation of a Palestinian state. Unilateral action by the US will likely push it further away.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.3. Pro: The Israeli government has [emphasized in the past](https://www.alaraby.co.uk/english/news/2016/11/7/israel-rejects-french-peace-initiative-again), and the Israeli public has stated in surveys \([PSR, p. 7](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)\), that the preferred method of engaging with the Palestinians is through bilateral talks. Thus, the involvement of and pressure from third actors will likely be received negatively.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.3.1. Con: Recognition does not constitute involvement in the talks. Thus, it is fully compatible with bilateral talks between Israel and Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4. Con: US recognition of Palestine might get Israel back to the negotiation table by signaling disapproval of current Israeli policies on the peace process. This can encourage the Israeli public to question its government's stance, as that is leading to increasing international isolation.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.1. Pro: More than half of all Israelis believe that there are high or very high chances that the international community will impose sanctions on their country for its policies in the occupied territories. This indicates that the Israeli public is aware that it is running out of international sympathy \([IDI, p. 5](http://www.peaceindex.org/files/Peace_Index_Data_January_2016-Eng.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.1.1. Pro: This aligns with public opinion in the US: almost half of all Americans support the so far unprecedented step of imposing sanctions in reaction to new settlements \([Brookings, p. 21](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/cmep_20161202_public_opinion_poll.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.2. Con: The majority of Israelis believe that their country should not take the international community's criticism towards its policy in the occupied territories seriously into account. The country will thus probably not be responsive to a change in the American position on these issues \([IDI, p. 4](http://www.peaceindex.org/files/Peace_Index_Data_January_2016-Eng.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.3. Con: More than eight out of ten Israelis believe that the international community's criticism towards Israel's policies in the occupied territories is biased in favor of Palestinian interests. It is thus unlikely that criticism will be well-received \([IDI, p. 4](http://www.peaceindex.org/files/Peace_Index_Data_January_2016-Eng.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.3.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5. Con: The United States would not lose much by alienating Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.1. Con: Israel is one of the [most prolific](https://www.sipri.org/research/armament-and-disarmament/arms-transfers-and-military-spending/arms-production) exporters of arms. In the past, the US was able to influence the targets of these exports, for example by blocking sales [to China](http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2005/06/27/AR2005062700351.html). This leverage might be lost if relations with Israel deteriorate.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.2. Pro: The extent and unconditionality of American support for Israel has been described as going against America's strategic and moral interests, and as being primarily the result of strong lobbying \([Mearsheimer/Walt, p. 335f.](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=2iUdyQs_NhYC&printsec=frontcover&dq=The+Israel+Lobby+and+American+Foreign+Policy&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiP6LCW2c_TAhUMbrwKHfvZBH0Q6AEIJTAA)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.2.1. Pro: In terms of the funding it provides to members of Congress, the Pro-Israel lobby ranks [among the top 25](https://www.opensecrets.org/industries/mems.php), far above any other country-specific lobby group in the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.2.2. Pro: As of 2015, and according to a survey among Washington insiders, the influence of the Pro-Israel lobby on American politics was [amongst the top five](http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/content/article/2005/05/18/AR2005051802143.html), along with national organizations such as the NRA and the American Association of Retired Persons \(AARP\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.2.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.4.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3. Con: If the United States were to distance itself from Israel, this could be interpreted as the abandonment of a close ally - and especially so in other countries allied with and dependent on US support, like South Korea and Taiwan. America's system of alliances could therefore suffer.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.1. Con: America retains the ability to simultaneously denounce Israel for its actions yet reaffirm its commitment to its relations with other countries.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.1.1. Con: When the United States recognized China in the 1970s, this was perceived as a de-facto abandonment of Taiwan. Even though the US reaffirmed its commitment to other allies, several of them were shocked and opted for less reliance on America in their security affairs \([Overholt, p. 710f.](http://www.theoverholtgroup.com/media/Articles-China/PresidentNixons-Trip-to-China-and-Its-Consequences-Asian-Survey-jstor.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.1.2. Con: The US has [affirmed](http://thehill.com/blogs/floor-action/senate/212617-senate-passes-resolution-in-support-of-israel) its support for Israel [many times](https://www.wsj.com/articles/in-speech-to-aipac-donald-trump-affirms-support-for-israel-1458605471) in the past. A move like this would indicate that affirmations of support on the part of the US are worth little, and do not necessarily indicate underlying US policy.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.2. Pro: [Recent events](http://www.npr.org/2016/07/23/487151465/casting-doubt-on-u-s-commitment-to-mutual-defense-donald-trump-unsettles-nato-al) have cast doubt on the US's loyalty and commitment to longstanding alliances. This move would reinforce and deepen an existing distrust of the US's reliability.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.3. Pro: President Obama [spoke of](http://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=91150432) an "unshakeable commitment to Israel's security". Recognizing Palestine could be interpreted as a weakening of this commitment to American allies.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.3.3.1. Con: The US can recognise Palestine without compromising its commitment to Israel's security - defence pledges and aid deals will still remain.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.4. Pro: Israel is not even among the [top-20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_largest_trading_partners_of_the_United_States) of America's trade partners measured in trade volume.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.5. Pro: Israel is not even among the [top-20](http://travel.trade.gov/view/m-2016-I-001/index.asp) origins of tourists visiting the United States. Countries of comparable size, like Sweden and Switzerland, outrank it.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.6. Pro: Israel has [no US military bases](http://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2015/06/us-military-bases-around-the-world-119321), whereas regional players with poor historic relations with Israel \(like Jordan and Turkey\) do have US bases. A deterioration in the Israeli-US relationship would not affect US capacity to project power regionally.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.7. Pro: A less close relationship with Israel might be appreciated by the American public: 37% believe that Israel has too much influence on US politics, although the plurality believes it has the right amount of influence \([Brookings, p. 4](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.7.1. Con: In a Republican-dominated era, the opinions of Republican voters are most influential. The majority of them believe that Israel has the right amount of influence \([Brookings, p. 4](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.8. Pro: This could result in less aid provided to Israel, freeing up funds that could be spent elsewhere.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.8.1. Pro: The US has spent almost $100 billion on Foreign Military Financing \(FMF\) since 1985 [\(CRS p.22\)](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33476.pdf).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.8.1.1. Con: FMF payments are meant to enable foreign governments to purchase American military products and services. The money therefore comes back home and supports the US economy.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.8.1.1.1. Con: Israel is allowed to convert about a quarter of this military aid into shekels to spend at home \([CRS, p. 2](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.8.1.1.1.1. Con: The provision that allows Israel to spend 26% of military aid domestically is being [phased out](http://www.cnbc.com/2016/09/15/big-us-military-aid-package-to-israel-has-strings-attached.html) over the next five years, requiring Israel to spend all military aid within the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6. Pro: Israel could sell sensitive military technology that either the US shares with it or it creates itself in retaliation for US recognition.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.1. Pro: It was upon Washington's insistence that Israel agreed to terminate the sale of problematic weapons and military technology to China and deprive itself of both a major market for its world-class military exports and a source of influence with Beijing. Without this pressure, Israel would resume selling weapons to China \([Blackwill, p. 9](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/pubs/Blackwill-Slocombe_Report.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.2. Con: Due to Israel's reliance on American support for equipping its military, it is unlikely that Israel would endanger this support by going against its supplier's interests.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.6.2.3.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.1.5.2.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.3. Pro: Israel has a track record of selling US arms to third countries without authorization. This was the case in the 1980s when it sold cluster bombs to Ethiopia and in 1999 when it sold drone technology to [China](http://forward.com/news/2501/china-crisis-straining-us-israel-ties/) \([Clarke, p. 95](https://www.jstor.org/stable/1149008?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.4. Pro: The US shares sensitive military technology with Israel , such as F-35 aircraft \([Sharp, p. 12](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/mideast/RL33222.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.4.1. Con: Presumably, the US would stop sharing sensitive technology with Israel if the latter started selling it as a form of retaliation for the recognition of Palestine.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.5. Con: Selling sensitive military technology would hurt Israel as much as the US, as Israel shares many of the same enemies. This would make intentional leaking of technology unlikely.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.5.1. Con: While US relations with Russia are at their [lowest point](http://nationalpost.com/news/world/putin-says-u-s-russia-relations-at-lowest-point-since-cold-war-asks-american-business-leaders-to-help-trump/wcm/06d1cab2-109e-4677-88e3-ed3b7a21fc8d) since the Cold War, Israeli relations with Russia are the [warmest](http://www.jpost.com/Israel-News/Despite-Syria-Israel-Russia-relations-are-the-warmest-in-history-485062) they have ever been, despite conflicting goals in Syria.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.6.5.2. Con: While relations between the US and China are growing [worse](http://www.realclearworld.com/articles/2017/04/06/6_reasons_us-china_relations_are_headed_for_trouble_112279.html) over conflicting priorities of trade and security, Israel and China have [vowed](http://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy-defence/article/2080572/china-and-israel-vow-deepen-relations) to deepen relations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7. Pro: A deterioration in Israel-US relations will jeopardize America's operations and presence in the region.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.1. Con: Countries like Saudi Arabia, Egypt, Qatar, Kuwait or the UAE find it difficult to [side with the US](https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB116433750279531793) publicly on Iran unless "Washington pressures Israel on a peace initiative". If anything, recognition increases regional cooperation with the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.1.1. Con: The US already [shares intelligence](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-saudi-yemen-exclusive-idUSKBN0N129W20150411) and [sells weapons](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-saudi-defense-congress-idUSKCN11R2LU) to Saudi Arabia, independent of the situation in Palestine. Regional cooperation and a Palestinian peace deal are not linked.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.1.2. Con: The US is [seeking](http://www.timesofisrael.com/us-looks-to-form-arab-alliance-against-iran-report/) to form an anti-Iran coalition with Arab states that would share intelligence with Israel as well. A peace deal is not required for Arab nations to cooperate with the US when their interests align.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.1.3. Con: Saudi Arabia, Qatar and the UAE have a strong anti-Iran position [due to sectarian tensions](http://www.spiegel.de/international/world/saudia-arabia-iran-and-the-new-middle-eastern-cold-war-a-1090725.html). The US does not need to pressure them for support.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.2. Pro: Israel hosts a large-scale American [war reserve stock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_reserve_stock#War_Reserves_Stock_Allies-Israel) with some $1.8 billion worth of equipment for use in case of armed conflict in the region.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.3. Pro: Israel is a world leader in the development of unmanned aerial systems, for both intelligence collection and combat, and it has shared with the U.S. military the technology, the doctrine, and its experience regarding these systems \([Blackwill, p. 10](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/pubs/Blackwill-Slocombe_Report.pdf)\). America's ability to gather intelligence could be restricted if Israel decided to cut of trade in military technology.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.3.1. Pro: The US [relies](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/u-s-israel-intelligence-collaboration) on Israel for crucial intelligence about Hamas, Hezbollah, and al-Qaeda and its affiliate groups \([Blackwill, p. 11](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/pubs/Blackwill-Slocombe_Report.pdf)\) in the region. Deterioration of relations could put this intelligence cooperation at risk.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.3.1.1. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.3.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.3.1.2. Con: Intelligence about Hamas and Hezbollah is of relevance for the US only insofar as it helps to protect Israel. Neither organization targets America.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4. Pro: Israel is [strongly opposed](http://nationalinterest.org/feature/israels-master-plan-crush-irans-nuclear-program-13392) to the Iran nuclear deal. If Israeli-US relations deteriorate as a result of US recognition of Palestine, Israel may launch a pre-emptive strike against Iran, raising the possibility of a regional war.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.1. Pro: The threat of Iran acquiring a 'break-out' weapon after ten years, when the Iran Nuclear deal expires, may lead Israel to [strike](http://www.ocregister.com/2015/07/26/why-israel-will-hit-iran-after-obamas-gone/) Iran, especially if it feels it is losing US support and must protect itself.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.2. Con: Amos Yadlin, the former head of IDF Intelligence, [claimed](http://www.timesofisrael.com/ex-idf-intel-chief-strike-on-iran-likely-wont-spark-regional-war/) that it was highly unlikely that a missile strike by Israel would lead to a regional war, primarily because Iran was aware of Israel's ability to destroy it in an all out war. This in turn would threaten the survival of the Iranian regime.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.3. Con: The Israeli military and intelligence community supports the Iran nuclear deal.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.3.1. Con: The Israeli political and security establishments are [split](http://nationalinterest.org/feature/netanyahu-idf-are-split-the-iran-nuclear-deal-15368?page=2) on their attitude towards the Iran deal. Despite the security establishment's acceptance of the Iran nuclear deal, Netanyahu could still order an attack on Iran.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.3.2. Pro: Official Israeli statements on Iran is nothing but political rhetoric. Multiple Israeli security officials, including Israeli Chief of the General Staff Lieutenant General Gadi Eizenkot, have [stated](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2016/03/iran-nuclear-deal-israel/472767/) that Iran's nuclear threat has been pushed back by at least 10-15 years, if not eliminated.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.3.3. Pro: The Israeli security establishment has [warned](http://www.al-monitor.com/pulse/originals/2017/01/israel-netanyahu-trump-security-iran-deal-nuke-agreement.html) Netanyahu to not touch the Iran nuclear deal. They assessed that destroying the nuclear deal will unite the Iranian people behind the regime, and possibly even push it to pursue an all out nuclear option.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.4.4. Pro: Israel [was close to](http://www.jpost.com/Israel-News/Politics-And-Diplomacy/Peres-bombshell-I-stopped-an-Israeli-strike-on-Iran-469112) preemptively striking Iran in the past. A falling out with the United States might embolden Israel to do so next time - and thereby torpedoing America's politics in the region, for example the 2015 nuclear deal with Iran.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.5. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.6.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.8. Con: Damaging its relationship with the US would isolate Israel in the international community. This isolation could set in motion a [diplomatic avalanche](http://www.timesofisrael.com/left-alone-at-un-israel-can-ignore-but-not-avoid-diplomatic-fallout/) that will ultimately weaken Israel’s position in negotiations with the Palestinians. Israel would not like this to happen.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.8.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.4.4.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9. Con: This might be a positive outcome; its close association with Israel is a burden for the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.1. Con: The [majority of Americans](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) do not perceive Israel as a burden to the United States.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.1.1. Con: The public is not always aware of the intricacies of international politics, and is thus unlikely to be aware of the cost to their country of such a close association with Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.1.2. Pro: Even if the actual benefits are hard to quantify, three out of four Americans believe that Israel provides "essential military and intelligence cooperation" for the United States in the region \([Brookings, p. 38](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/cmep_20161202_public_opinion_poll.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.1.2.1. Con: This is not proof of Israel actually providing essential military and intelligence cooperation. Geo-strategic security policies are not made on \(often\) misplaced public belief.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.5.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.3. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.7.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4. Pro: The negative perception of Israel's defiance of international law, occupation of Palestinian territories and military engagements with surrounding countries, reflects poorly on the US as the "[principal enabler](http://www.theamericanconservative.com/articles/americas-misadventures-in-the-middle-east/)" of this behavior.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.1. Pro: In Germany, about as many people have a negative as have a positive opinion about Israel. The [most common attributes](https://de.statista.com/statistik/daten/studie/226525/umfrage/umfrage-zum-bild-der-deutschen-von-israel/) associated with Israel by the majority of Germans are ruthlessness and aggressiveness \([Bertelsmann, p. 31](https://www.bertelsmann-stiftung.de/fileadmin/files/BSt/Publikationen/GrauePublikationen/Studie_LW_Germany_and_Israel_today_2015.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.2.3.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.3. Pro: In a BBC poll on the international perception of various countries, Israel was among the most negatively viewed ones, ahead of only North Korea, Pakistan and Iran \([BBC, p. 4](http://downloads.bbc.co.uk/mediacentre/country-rating-poll.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.4. Con: National interests often override potential public relations damage. Else the US would not have routinely supported [regimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_authoritarian_regimes_supported_by_the_United_States) that are far worse and unpopular than Israel, from Pinochet in Chile to Marcos in the Phillipines and King Abdullah in Saudi Arabia.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.5. Pro: Recognizing Palestine, and thus taking a more moderate stance on the conflict, would serve to dissociate the US from Israel's actions.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6. Con: The negative views cited here aren't simply because of Israel's defiance of international law, but relate to Israel's perception on the whole. Because of continued widespread anti-Semitism, and because of the link between anti-Semitism and negative perceptions of Israel, the U.S should not use these negative perceptions to guide their own actions.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.1. Pro: Anti-semitism is still widespread in [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antisemitism_in_Europe#Public_opinion_polls).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.2. Pro: Empirical [studies](https://www.uni-marburg.de/fb03/politikwissenschaft/methoden/team/heyder/criticism_of_israel_vs_anti_semitism_2005_english.pdf) that seek to separate and analyze views about Jews and views about Israel find that negative attitudes towards Israel often function as "communicational detours"  to get around norms against expressing anti-Semitic views.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.2.1. Pro: It is crucial to note that this does not imply that all criticism or negative perceptions about Israel stem from anti-Semitism, but merely that widespread anti-Semitism contributes to negative views about Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.3. Pro: To the extent that these negative perceptions are formed by underlying anti-Semitic prejudices, it would be immoral to buckle under pressure resulting from these prejudices.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.4. Pro: To the extent that these negative perceptions are formed by underlying prejudices rather than Israel's actions towards Palestine, and given that the United States will still be close to Israel on many issues despite recognising Palestine, it is unlikely that simply recognizing Palestine as a state will change any reputational damage that the U.S. suffers from its association with Israel.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.6.4.1. Con: This will be perceived not just as a dissociation from Israel's actions towards Palestine, but also as a general repudiation of Israel as an actor. So even if negative perceptions of Israel are based on anti-Semitism, the US's image will improve.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.7. Con: Given the US' long history of unwavering support for Israel, one largely symbolic move by a single administration wouldn't substantially affect perception of the US.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8. Con: These negative perceptions of Israel do not exist in a vacuum and should at least be taken with a grain of salt, as they might be based on biased reporting in the media.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.1. Pro: Researchers [argue](https://www.welt.de/print/die_welt/politik/article130459269/Ein-Grossteil-deutscher-Medien-berichtet-voreingenommen.html) [that](http://www.zeit.de/politik/deutschland/2014-08/israel-medien-kritik) the German mainstream media tends to be far more critical and harder on Israel than on Palestine, especially when locating the fault for violence, and to even rely on antisemitic cliches in its reporting.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.2. Pro: A former reporter for the Associate Press in Jerusalem [argued that](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/11/how-the-media-makes-the-israel-story/383262/) the international media tends to assign blame for the region's conflict primarily to Israel, is being co-opted by its enemies and thereby became "an amplifier for the propaganda" of radical Palestinian forces.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.3. Pro: A study analyzing the reporting by Al-Arabiya \(Saudi Arabia\) and Al-Jazeera \(Qatar\) found that Palestinians are usually cast as victims and Israelis as aggressors. Palestinian perspectives and suffering are emphasized over the Israeli experience \([Elmasry et al., p. 750](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1748048513482545?journalCode=gazb)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.3.1. Con: This bias is hardly surprising and not representative as both media outlets are sponsored by governments that do not even accept Israeli passports on their territory.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.4. Pro: A 2003 report by the Washington Institute for Near East Policy found that various American television stations and newspapers report in a biased and ignorant fashion on the Israel-Palestine conflict, casting Israel as the sole aggressor and buying into the propaganda and lies of Palestinian radicals \([Muravchik, p. 113f.](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/pubs/CoveringtheIntifada.pdf.pdf)\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.4.8.4.1. Con: The Washington Institute for Near East Policy [was founded](http://foreignpolicy.com/2010/04/09/robert-satloff-doth-protest-too-much/) by the former President and Vice-President of the American Israel Public Affairs Committee \(AIPAC\), the country's largest pro-Israel lobbying group. Its publications should therefore be seen as agenda-driven.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.4.3.2.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.2.7.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.9.7. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4. Pro: Progress in the conflict between Israel and the Palestinians would weaken America's adversaries in the region.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.1. Pro: Hezbollah [was founded](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-middle-east-10814698) as an Islamic resistance movement against Israel and the United States. Hamas, equally, [was founded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas#Aims) as a resistance movement against Israel. Less hostile relations between Israel and Palestine would undermine the raison d'être of both organizations.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.1.1. Con: Hezbollah does little to threaten Israel or project Iranian power anymore. Its participation in the Syrian civil war has gotten it stuck [in a quagmire](http://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/opeds/Levitt20140911-PRISM.pdf); Israel [considers](https://www.middleeastmonitor.com/20170223-hezbollah-and-hamas-are-too-weak-to-fight-says-israel-army-chief/) neither Hezbollah nor Hamas capable of putting up a fight at this time.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.1.1.1. Con: The war-fighting experience Hezbollah has gained in the Syrian Civil War, as well as the huge number of weapons it has captured or been provided with, has actually put it in a [much stronger position](https://www.wsj.com/articles/syrias-civil-war-produces-a-clear-winner-hezbollah-1491173790) to fight Israel in the future.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.1.2. Con: There is no amount of "less hostile relations" that would sate the Hamas. They [do not want a two-state solution](http://www.aljazeera.com/programmes/upfront/2017/01/hamas-state-solution-charter-170127121227513.html), they want an Israel-free solution.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2. Pro: Better relations between Israel and the Palestinians would weaken Iran, one of the principal adversaries of the United States, which has long used Hezbollah and Hamas [as proxies.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict)
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.1. Pro: Support for terrorist groups [allows](https://www.lawfareblog.com/irans-support-terrorist-groups) Iran to undermine and intimidate rivals, influence the Israel-Palestine conflict, disrupt peace negotiations, and project power in regional crises. Weakening Iran's proxies, such as Hezbollah, would weaken the ability of Iran to carry out these disruptive actions.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.1.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.2. Pro: According to Prime Minister Netanyahu, defense analysts in Israel [estimate that](http://www.timesofisrael.com/netanyahu-80-of-security-threats-against-israel-emanate-from-iran/) more than 80% of the country's security problems emanate from Iran.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.3. Con: Recent efforts at cooperation, for example through the 2015 nuclear deal and the rise of common enemies like the Islamic State, call into question whether relations between the US and Iran are still as hostile as they were in the past.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.3.1. Con: Iran is one of the very few countries without a US embassy. This is only the case in extraordinary circumstances \(e.g. in Taiwan\) or because of very bad relations \(e.g. with North Korea and Iran\).
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.4. Con: Iran's [raison d'être](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/8007/iran-palestinian-state) for funding militant groups in Palestine such as Islamic Jihad is to kill Jews and destroy Israel. A peace deal will not stop Iran from continuing to fund militant groups.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.4.1. Con: However, a peace deal will reduce public support for militant groups as there will no longer be a reason to advocate for militancy. This will weaken the position of Iranian funded militant groups.
1.1.1.3.1.4.6.4.2.4.1.1. Pro: Hamas's ability to militarily resist Israel is dependent on its ability to [operate amongst civilians](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2014/jul/24/gaza-hamas-fighters-military-bases-guerrilla-war-civilians-israel-idf) in the Gaza Strip.

1.1.1.3.1.6. Pro: Various international and Israeli courts have found the occupation of Palestinian territories by Israel to be illegal.
1.1.1.3.1.6.1. Pro: The International Court of Justice found that Israel effectively '[annexed](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law/9780199588893.001.0001/law-9780199588893-chapter-8)' East Jerusalem with the 1980 Jerusalem Law.
1.1.1.3.1.6.1.1. Con: In 1980, a [legal opinion](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law/9780199588893.001.0001/law-9780199588893-chapter-8) argued that the extension of Israeli law over East Jerusalem did not equate to annexation. Israel had not annexed East Jerusalem, but merely extended its norms and laws over the eastern half of the city.
