Pro: Textually, God explicitly limited this promise to the seed of Isaac \([Gen 21:10](https://www.chabad.org/library/bible_cdo/aid/8216#v=10) as endorsed by [21:12](https://www.chabad.org/library/bible_cdo/aid/8216#v=12) and [25:5](https://www.chabad.org/library/bible_cdo/aid/8220/jewish/Chapter-25.htm#v=5)\). This promise was then given to Jacob and his descendants \([Gen 28:4](https://www.chabad.org/library/bible_cdo/aid/8223#v=4)\).
1.2.1.3. Con: Holy texts [like the Bible](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historicity_of_the_Bible#Schools_of_archaeological_and_historical_thought) are not a good source to base modern land claims upon as they are notoriously unreliable and usually perceived to be not rooted in historic facts.
1.2.1.3.1. Pro: International law is not based on religious justifications, as there is no way of evaluating such claims.
1.2.1.3.2. Con: Who cares about perception? Facts are all that matters. 1\) The claim is a strawman; modern zionists do not base their claim to the land of Israel on the Abrahamic covenant. The claim is based in part on [accepted history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arch_of_Titus) and [proven archeology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Dan_Stele). 2\) Though it is a strawman ostensibly to be demolished, the argument is false. Far from being notoriously unreliable, Biblical claims are in fact [very reliable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siloam_inscription#Translation) in [historical fact](http://blog.dovidgottlieb.com/search/label/Biblical%20archaeology) where it is relevant to land claims.
1.2.1.3.3. Con: When the [holy](http://corpus.quran.com/translation.jsp?chapter=5&verse=21) [texts](http://corpus.quran.com/translation.jsp?chapter=17&verse=104) of each party to a dispute [agree](http://blogs.timesofisrael.com/islam-supports-israels-right-of-existence/), then it would be advantageous to use this as a basis to resolve the dispute. For example both the Quran and the Bible agree that the land of Israel belongs to the Jewish nation, who will eventually return.
1.2.1.4. Con: The claims in a religious text have no moral significance for ownership because the religions espoused within those texts are not true.
1.2.1.5. Pro: [Psalm 137](http://www.israelnationalnews.com/Articles/Article.aspx/11981) commands Jews to never forget about Jerusalem.
1.2.1.6. Con: The number of followers a religion has tells us nothing about whether this religion's beliefs are more correct or relevant than any other religion's beliefs.
1.2.1.7. Pro: The Old Testament delineates the land of Israel in [Numbers 34:1-35:8](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Numbers%2034-35:8) and [Ezekiel 47:13-23](http://www.biblica.com/bible/online-bible/?osis=niv:Ezekiel.47:13%E2%80%9320:13).
1.2.1.7.1. Con: This extract \([Numbers 34:1-35:8](https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Numbers%2034-35:8)\) says "Six of the towns you give the Levites will be cities of refuge, to which a person who has killed someone may flee," which is not respected nowadays, so what was once, no longer is.
1.2.1.8. Con: Just because many people hold a belief does not make it true. Billions of people used to believe that the Earth is flat.
1.2.2. Pro: Some [Muslim scholars](http://www.meforum.org/2464/quran-covenant-with-jewish-people) even assign the Land of Israel \(including modern day Palestine\) to the Jews.
1.2.2.1. Pro: In [Qur'an 5:21](https://quran.com/5/21) Moses declares: "O my people, enter the Holy Land which Allah has assigned to you and do not turn back \[from fighting in Allah 's cause\] and \[thus\] become losers."
1.2.2.1.1. Con: This verse does not define the location, boundaries or borders of such a “Holy Land”, and does not state whether this land has been “assigned” for a specific period of time, or for eternity.
1.2.2.1.2. Con: Muslims believe that Moses was Muslim, and therefore one could make an argument that this “Holy Land” should now be under Muslim control.
1.2.2.2. Con: The Jewish Holy Torah recognizes that the land of Israel was the home for other and older tribes before the Israelites arrived : the Amorites and the Canaanites, the Hittites and the Perizzites, the Hivvites and the Jebusites. 
[Pentateuch Shemot 34:11-12](https://www.chabad.org/library/bible_cdo/aid/9895/jewish/Chapter-34.htm)
Thus according to the Torah, the Israelites descendants are not the most ancient inhabitants.
1.2.3. Con: Jerusalem is of great religious significance to Muslims, and is considered to be the [third holiest site](http://www.pij.org/details.php?id=646) in Islam.
1.2.3.1. Pro: Jerusalem was the first [qibla](https://www.al-islam.org/the-message-ayatullah-jafar-subhani/chapter-29-change-qiblah), or direction of prayer, for Muslims, before the qibla became Mecca.
1.2.3.2. Pro: It is the city from where Muhammad [ascended](http://www.jerusalem.com/articles/islam/muhammads_night_journey_to_jerusalem-a6295) to heaven and met Allah. It is an important religious event that is [celebrated](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2014/05/27/lailat-al-miraj-2014_n_5395082.html) by Muslims every year throughout the world.
1.2.3.3. Con: Jerusalem [appears](http://www.danielpipes.org/84/the-muslim-claim-to-jerusalem) in the Hebrew Bible 669 times and Zion \(which usually means Jerusalem, sometimes the Land of Israel\) 154 times, or 823 times in all. The Christian Bible mentions Jerusalem 154 times and Zion 7 times. Yet the Quran does not mention it once.
1.2.3.3.1. Con: Even though the Quran does not mention Jerusalem itself, it [refers to](https://quran.com/17/1) the Al-Aqsa Mosque in Jerusalem's old town.
1.2.3.3.2. Con: It is questionable whether references in holy scriptures are the appropriate standard to judge religious significance. The Bible does not mention the Vatican, the Pope or cardinals at any point, yet these stand at the center of the Catholic Church.
1.2.3.4. Con: Jerusalem has historically been used as a [political tool](http://www.danielpipes.org/84/the-muslim-claim-to-jerusalem) by Islamic empires. There is little religious importance affiliated with the city that outweighs Judaism's three thousand year old connection.
1.2.4. Pro: In ancient times the West Bank was part of Israel for a millennia starting with the [Kingdom of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_\(united_monarchy\)) in 1050 BCE to the [Herodian Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herodian_kingdom) 4 BCE. Indeed, Jews led the first independent polity in the region.
1.2.4.1. Pro: Unlike the existence of an ancient Jewish sovereign over this land, there has never been a Palestinian state, nor, until recently, did Palestinians have a separate identity. They saw themselves as part of a larger Arab Syria \([Bard, p. 3](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/jsource/images/mf2017.pdf#page=43)\).
1.2.4.1.1. Con: Accounts of past Jewish sovereignty on the disputed territories are based on historical accounts not backed up by research and archaeological evidence.
1.2.4.1.1.1. Pro: There is [a lack of archaeological evidence](http://www.haaretz.com/jewish/archaeology/.premium-1.575418) for the existence of King David. The stories of who he was and what he did are conflicting and give no coherent account.
1.2.4.1.1.1.1. Con: The [Tel Dan Inscription](https://www.biblicalarchaeology.org/daily/biblical-artifacts/artifacts-and-the-bible/the-tel-dan-inscription-the-first-historical-evidence-of-the-king-david-bible-story/) is strong evidence for the existence of King David that is taken seriously by modern scholars.
1.2.4.1.1.1.2. Con: King David’s palace is the best explanation for the discovery of the [Large Stone Structure](https://www.biblicalarchaeology.org/daily/biblical-sites-places/jerusalem/did-i-find-king-davids-palace/) discovered by Eilat Mazar.
1.2.4.1.1.2. Pro: The biblical accounts of King Solomon and the empire he ruled have been [called into question](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon#Historicity). Little archaeological evidence has been found for the power he is usually ascribed or [for the temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solomon%27s_Temple#Archaeology) in Jerusalem named after him.
1.2.4.1.1.3. Pro: The historical evidence for the [Kingdom of Judah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Judah#Archaeological_record) and the [Kingdom of Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Israel_\(united_monarchy\)#Archaeological_record) is sparse and disputed; both were likely much smaller, less unified and less powerful than depicted in biblical accounts.
1.2.4.1.1.4. Con: While aspects of the story by which the Jewish people trace their ancient claim to sovereignty in Israel and Palestine are questionable, others are not. For example, the historical and archeological evidence of the [Hasmonean Dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasmonean_dynasty) which ruled that area just prior to its incorporation into the Roman empire, is clear.
1.2.4.1.2. Con: Even if Palestinians understood their identity \(and by extension their nationality\) as part of a larger whole, this doesn't speak against their right to self-determination, which is at the basis of any claim to sovereignty. Thus, it is misleading to imply that there is no claim to Palestinian sovereignty over territory that Palestinians have occupied for centuries.
1.2.4.2. Con: -> See 1.2.4.1.1.
1.2.4.3. Con: The Israeli claims are based on periods of Jewish sovereignty almost 2000 years ago. This is hardly a convincing standard for present-day claims.
1.2.4.3.1. Pro: By the same logic, the Egyptian people have an exclusive claim to much of the territory as they had incorporated it [into their empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Egypt) by the 15th century BC already.
1.2.4.3.2. Pro: There is little reason to assume that first occupancy is more relevant for judging contemporary claims than the duration of occupancy. The Jews ruled over the territory in question for less than 250 years. Arabs have a history of living there for more than 1000 years.
1.2.4.3.3. Pro: Indeed, all else being equal, present-day claims should weight more recent periods of sovereignty over more ancient ones, since they relate more proximally to the present day world.
1.2.4.3.3.1. Con: The other way round, one could also justify Israel's rule over the territories it acquired over the course of the past decades from the Palestinians as its claims are more proximally to the present day.
1.2.4.4. Con: Even [during the period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Palestine#Independent_Canaanite.2C_Israelite_and_Philistine_period) with an Israelite presence in the region, other independent peoples were present. Thus, they should also have a claim to the land. Among them are the Philistines who [fought Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philistines) according to the Bible.
1.2.5. Con: Only 14% of Israelis regard the claim to a 'Greater Israel' as a priority \([Joint Palestinian-EU poll, p. 14](http://www.pcpsr.org/sites/default/files/Table%20of%20Findings_English%20Joint%20Poll%20Dec%202016_12Feb2017.pdf)\).
1.2.5.1. Con: Today, organisations close to the old Movement for Greater Israel, such as the [Yesha Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yesha_Council), have political influence.
1.2.6. Con: Palestinians have a strong moral claim to a Palestinian state given that they lived in the geographic area of Greater Palestine for centuries before leaving or [being expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus#Changes_in_the_Israeli_Representation_of_the_Causes_for_the_Exodus_.E2.80.93_Late_1970s) in response to the establishment of Israel.
1.2.6.1. Con: Before the [program of expulsion](http://www.meforum.org/263/why-jews-fled-the-arab-countries) from Arab countries, including Palestine, Jews were living in this territory too.
1.2.6.1.1. Con: The claim of the Jews is not incompatible with the claim of the Palestinians. The might both have legitimate claims and therefore both have states recognised.
1.2.6.2. Con: There was never a Palestinian state in history so they have no claim over the area.
1.2.6.2.1. Con: This should not matter if it is good for peace in the region.
1.2.6.2.1.1. Con: There is something to be said for this, but it's not good for peace in the region. When given land and self government, they elected terrorists and attacked Israel.
1.2.6.2.2. Con: Sovereign states as we know them today are relativily recent. There were almost no sovereign state in africa before the 1950s-1960s, it doesn't mean there were no people living there.
1.2.6.3. Con: [Israel's Proclamation of Independence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Declaration_of_Independence), issued May 14, 1948, invited the Palestinians to remain in their homes and become equal citizens in the new state.
1.2.6.4. Con: Several [binding instruments](http://avalon.law.yale.edu/20th_century/palmanda.asp) of international law grant sovereign rights to the Jewish people in the land of Israel. Zero binding instruments of international law support the claims of the Palestinian Arabs.
1.2.6.5. Con: There may be a claim but it is neither strong nor moral. As history attests, Jews were the original inhabitants- [dispossessed and exiled by the Romans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Roman_Empire#Dispersion_of_the_Jews_in_the_Roman_Empire) in the 1st century and the land then invaded and occupied by several succeeding empires. [Arabs invaded in the 7th century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant#Conquest_of_Palestine). The claim of the Palestinian Arabs is based on the principle that the descendants of invaders and occupiers have a greater right to inherit property than the descendents of the original owners.
1.2.7. Con: Under the plan proposed here, Jews would retain access to their most important religious sites, such as the Temple Mount and the Wailing Wall in Jerusalem. A two-state solution can thus accommodate the religious claims of Jews.
1.2.7.1. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.4.
1.2.8. Con: Religious claims played very [little](https://www.theatlantic.com/past/docs/unbound/bookauth/zionism/gwint.htm) role in the early history of the Zionist movement in Palestine and in the creation of the state of Israel, during which time Zionism was aggressively secular. Rather, the chief argument for sovereignty was the need to have a Jewish majority nation-state in order to enforce the rights of Jewish people.
1.2.9. Con: If ancient claims to land are valid, the rightful rulers of nearly all nations would need to change.
1.2.9.1. Con: Even if true on paper, this would not matter in practice as there is no dispute over the rightful rulers of most swathes of land. The slippery slope hinted at by the parent is therefore not of practical relevance for recognizing Jewish land claims.
1.2.10. Con: The United States is a secular democracy and should not take religious claims into consideration when deciding a matter of foreign policy.
1.2.10.1. Con: When making a decision that has an impact on a highly religious area of the world, it would be foolish to ignore religion entirely.
1.2.11. Con: The Jews are not the first settlers, nor the founders, nor the people who inhabited that land for the longest period. If ancient claims are to be considered, then the descendants of the Canaanites - the native Levantines - Palestinians, Lebanese, Syrians, as proven by genetic studies [\(1\)](https://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2008/10/081030-phoenician-dna-genographic-missions.html)[\(2\)](https://anthropology.net/2008/10/30/the-y-chromosomal-footprint-of-phoenicians-throughout-the-mediterranean/)[\(3\)](http://www.sciencemag.org/news/2017/07/ancient-dna-reveals-fate-mysterious-canaanites), would be the real first settlers and founders of Jerusalem and other cities, and should own that land. If religious claims are to be considered, then we should consider Muslim claims too.
1.2.11.1. Pro: All this about moving the Embassy is nothing but political pandering to dispensational evangelicals that believe political Israel are God's chosen.
1.2.11.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.2.2.
1.2.12. Con: Religious claims can't determine the "rightful rulers" of a land. The Amerindian people have a [strong religion](http://nativeamericannetroots.net/diary/315) and [worship specific places](http://indianrockpiles.weetu.com/articles/IndianRockPiles.html) on the Land of the United States of America and Canada, yet [they are not](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pr2CljnycW4) its rulers. A similar situation exists in many other countries and regions.
1.2.13. Con: The Zionist movement was predominately European Jewish. The original Jews that were expelled and wish to return to the area did return and then [converted to islam](https://mondediplo.com/2008/09/07israel) - they are modern day Palestinians.
1.2.13.1. Con: Sand's thesis rests on a number of claims, one of which is the idea of Khazar myth. It has been [refuted \(part 5, conclusions\)](http://www.khazaria.com/khazar-diaspora.html) and [debunked](https://www.haaretz.com/jewish/khazar-myth-busted-1.5253397) a number of times.
1.2.13.1.1. Pro: A number of [comments](http://yaacovlozowick.blogspot.com/2010/09/scholars-on-shlomo-sand.html?showComment=1285184760358#c555239050575930416), [articles](http://jewlicious.com/2009/11/shlomo-sand-ridiculed-by-historian-simon-schama/) [and](http://jewlicious.com/2009/03/the-french-love-a-good-anti-zionist-socialist-book/) [reviews](http://jewlicious.com/2009/03/french-love-a-good-anti-zionist-book-cont/) have attacked his [methods](https://newrepublic.com/article/72363/indecent-proposal) and [conclusions](http://zioncon.blogspot.com/2008/08/tel-aviv-universitys-shlomo-sand-and.html) \(though some articles are behind [paywalls](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1080/13531040902752531?journalCode=fjih20)\).
1.2.14. Con: -> See 1.2.2.2.
1.3. Pro: Public opinion in the US supports this step: [more Americans](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) support an independent Palestinian state than oppose it.
1.3.1. Con: At the same time, [two thirds of Americans](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx) sympathize more with Israel than with Palestinians in the current situation; only 15% think the other way around. This makes the recognition of Palestine against Israel's explicit preference hard to sell.
1.3.1.1. Pro: The public's attitude towards Israel gives American politicians little incentive to support positions that run counter to Israeli interests. In fact, support for Israel has been labeled as "cheap talk" - it gives politicians large benefits with minimal risk \([Cavari/Nyer, p. 20](https://www.jstor.org/stable/pdf/10.2979/israelstudies.19.3.1.pdf)\).
1.3.1.2. Pro: The [vast majority](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/05/23/5-facts-about-how-americans-view-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of Republican voters sympathize more with Israel than with Palestine and do not consider a peaceful two-state solution viable. Politicians in Republican-dominated US politics have little to gain from defying this.
1.3.1.3. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.3.2.
1.3.1.4. Con: Sympathising with Israel is not mutually exclusive to establishing a Palestinian state. The American public can blame Hamas for its aggressive actions but still believe that the Palestinian people deserve a state.
1.3.1.5. Pro: In the same vein, only a very small minority [of 6%](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) would like to see the Trump government lean towards the Palestinian side in this conflict.
1.3.1.5.1. Con: This is only because the majority of voters want the Trump administration to lean towards [neither side](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/), so this does not indicate a general attitude of support for Israel.
1.3.1.6. Pro: Almost half of all Americans - and a majority of Republican voters - believe that the Jewish people are God's chosen people. This makes policies perceived as going against Israeli interests hard to sell \([Brookings, p. 9](https://www.brookings.edu/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2015-Poll-Key-Findings-Final-1.pdf)\).
1.3.2. Con: While this is currently the case, support for Israel is increasing and support for a Palestinian state is decreasing over time; given that the current margin in favour of a Palestinian state is small, it is likely to disappear in the future. \([Gallup](http://www.gallup.com/poll/189626/americans-views-toward-israel-remain-firmly-positive.aspx)\)
1.3.2.1. Con: Policies are not based upon expected future voter preferences, but current actual voter preferences. Given that, the US should recognise Palestine as a state since a majority of the population supports it.
1.3.3. Con: The relevance and trustworthiness of American public opinion is questionable in light of how uninformed Americans generally are about foreign policy issues.
1.3.3.1. Pro: Only a third of Americans have ever heard of USAid, their country's own organization for international development. Even among college graduates this number increases to only 54% \([Milner/Tingley, p. 392](https://scholar.harvard.edu/dtingley/publications/public-opinion-and-foreign-aid-review-essay)\).
1.3.3.2. Pro: According to [polls](http://www.kff.org/global-health-policy/poll-finding/data-note-americans-views-on-the-u-s-role-in-global-health/), only one in twenty Americans knows that the United States spends about 1% of its GDP on foreign aid. The average estimate of the number is 26%.
1.3.3.3. Pro: Studies from the 1990s indicate that Americans are [less informed](http://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1081180X96001002003) about foreign policy issues and world affairs than citizens of major European countries and Canada.
1.3.3.4. Pro: Many Americans lack basic geographic knowledge about the world and especially the Middle East. In a 2016 survey of American university and college students, seven out of ten couldn't locate Israel on a map; only half were able to pinpoint countries of major relevance for US foreign policy like Iraq and Iran \([CFR, p. 23](https://www.cfr.org/content/newsletter/files/CFR_NatGeo_ASurveyonGlobalLiteracy.pdf)\).
1.3.3.4.1. Pro: These numbers are persistent and represent not only students. As of 2006, three out of four Americans couldn't locate Israel or Iran on a map of the region. Two thirds couldn't find major theaters of US engagement like Iraq or major allies like Saudi Arabia \([Roper, p. 25](https://www.nationalgeographic.com/roper2006/pdf/FINALReport2006GeogLitsurvey.pdf)\).
1.3.4. Pro: [Two thirds](https://www.brookings.edu/research/american-attitudes-on-the-israeli-palestinian-conflict/) of all Americans - and even almost half of all Republican voters - believe America should either support or at least not block a UN resolution that recognizes Palestine as a state.
1.3.4.1. Pro: Given the US's history of voting on the UN Security Council \(it has vetoed nearly every resolution unfavorable to Israel\), even an abstention would be a de facto endorsement of the resolution.
1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.
1.5. Pro: Recognition of a Palestinian state is an important step in ending Israeli occupation of Palestinian territories.
1.5.1. Pro: If Palestine is recognised as a state, [Israeli settlements](http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-middle-east-38888649) will be tantamount to violating the sovereignty of this newly formed state. This makes them less tenable, and likely to stop.

1.5.1.3. Pro: Israel recently [authorised](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/02/israel-authorises-3000-settler-homes-west-bank-170201051854191.html) 3,000 more settler homes in the West Bank. These will likely continue unless the Palestinian state is established.
1.5.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.
1.5.3. Pro: The US is one of the world's most influential actors. A US recognition of Palestine could be a powerful way of inspiring other nations to push harder for an independent Palestinian state.
1.5.3.1. Pro: By being the first big western country to [recognize](http://www.theperspective.se/?p=882) Palestine, Sweden led the way for a number of other Western European countries, including France, the United Kingdom and Spain, to do the same. US recognition would have even more effect, given its international status.
1.5.3.2. Con: The United States is too late to the boat to serve as an example to other nations, given that [70.5%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_State_of_Palestine) of nations already recognize Palestine.
1.5.4. Pro: The only way for the Palestinian people to escape their oppression is for them to achieve a semblance of political parity with Israel, which will only be achieved through  international recognition.

1.5.9. Pro: Recognizing Palestine would improve the work of the UN on the ground in the Palestinian territories.
1.5.9.1. Pro: Currently, UN organisations who work with Palestine can be penalised, as [UNESCO](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/nov/08/us-unesco-voting-funds-palestine-decision) was when the US withheld 22% of its budget when it admitted Palestine. This would no longer be the case if the US itself recognised Palestine.

1.5.9.2. Con: Even without membership in specific UN organizations, these can do work in Palestine. UNIDO, for example, runs several projects on [food safety](http://gtad.wto.org/trta_subcategory.aspx?cat=3311301) or for the [Marble stone](https://www.unido.org/fileadmin/user_media_upgrade/Resources/Evaluation/Palestine_TVET_Evaluation_Final_Report__.pdf) industry.
1.5.10. Pro: The UN Fact Finding Mission in Gaza found that "some of the actions of the Government of Israel might justify a competent court finding that crimes against humanity have been committed," for example the [naval blockade](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2011/10/20111030172356990380.html). \([UN, p. 284](http://www2.ohchr.org/english/bodies/hrcouncil/docs/12session/A-HRC-12-48.pdf)\). If Palestine were to be established as a sovereign state, these crimes would receive more attention and condemnation from the international community.
1.5.10.1. Con: The blockade is necessary to prevent Hamas from growing stronger.
1.5.10.1.1. Pro: Hamas uses the [majority of the supplies](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/israel-s-quot-blockade-quot-of-gaza) brought into Gaza, so they never reach civilians anyways.
1.5.10.1.2. Pro: The US has [imposed sanctions](http://www.haaretz.com/news/u-s-imposes-sanctions-on-gaza-institutions-over-hamas-links-1.264983) on Gazan institutions because it realises the link between Hamas and the region.
1.5.10.2. Con: An earlier report by the UN, the [Palmer Report](https://www.un.org/News/dh/infocus/middle_east/Gaza_Flotilla_Panel_Report.pdf) \(p. 44\), declared the naval blockade on Gaza legal.
1.5.10.2.1. Con: The Palmer Report was intended to [mend relations](https://foreignpolicy.com/2011/09/02/u-n-s-gaza-flotilla-report-adrift-at-sea/) between Turkey and Israel rather than provide a factual assessment of the situation. Not only was the report more political than factual in nature, it also relied exclusively on information provided by Turkey and Israel, hence its conclusions cannot be considered definitive in either fact or law.
1.5.10.3. Pro: The Gaza blockade is very harmful for the Palestinians living in Gaza, and should be lifted.
1.5.10.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.6.1.2.
1.5.10.3.2. Pro: The four-year blockade deprives 1.6 million Palestinians living in the enclave of fundamental human rights.
1.5.10.3.2.1. Pro: About one-third of Gaza's arable land and 85 percent of its fishing waters are totally or partially inaccessible due to [Israeli military measures](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-un-gaza-rights-idUSTRE78C59R20110913). As a result, at least two-thirds of Gazan households lack secure access to food.
1.5.10.3.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.3.1.1.1.7.
1.5.10.3.2.3. Con: The United Nations Relief and Work Agency \(UNRWA\) [suspended](http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2009-02/07/content_10776872.htm) its humanitarian activities in response to Hamas security forces seizing its aids. The blockade does not deprive Palestinians of important resources, but rather Hamas does.
1.5.10.3.2.3.1. Con: Hamas and Israel can both be responsible for depriving Palestinians of important resources. Just because Hamas steals some resources does not mean Israel does not harm Palestinians as well.
1.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.
1.7. Con: The diplomatic recognition of Palestine alone will do little to help resolve the long-running conflict between Israel and Palestine.
1.7.1. Con: There would be a higher chance that Israel would be held accountable for any unfair practices. Much would change.
1.7.2. Con: The recognition of Palestine as a state will not resolve the conflict but it might help. The US should do anything which might help resolve the conflict.
1.7.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.6.1.5.
1.7.4. Pro: The intractability of the conflict between Palestinians and Israel [has](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/0162-895X.00255/full) [been](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1540-4560.2007.00518.x/abstract) [linked](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1751-2409.2010.01018.x/abstract) to underlying emotions and collective emotional orientations that fuel thinking and beliefs which make any progress next to impossible.
1.7.4.1. Pro: Emotional orientations can strengthen existing beliefs and even function as internally-generated evidence in support of these beliefs. The resulting beliefs and dispositions can thus be largely immune to logical arguments \([Mercer, p. 7](https://www.jstor.org/stable/pdf/40607979.pdf?refreqid=excelsior%3A9d7e89b17ec5614b927244689024ed89)\).
1.7.5. Pro: In 2005, Israel unilaterally withdrew from Gaza, removing all its settlements. Instead of rebuilding Gaza, the territory was turned into a terrorist base for Hamas which began firing rockets into Israel and sending suicide bombers into Israel resulting in deaths of Israeli civilians. Assuming recognition will lead to withdrawal of Israel from the Palestinian territories, the same may happen again.
1.7.6. Pro: As the Palestinian leadership \(both [Hamas](https://www.timesofisrael.com/hamas-assures-critics-israels-destruction-still-a-goal/) and [Fatah](https://www.timesofisrael.com/hamas-assures-critics-israels-destruction-still-a-goal/)\) has been clear that an independent Palestine will not end the conflict, recognition of Palestine would simply reward Palestinian intransigence.
1.7.7. Con: Deciding whether or not a given population deserves independence as a basic human right should not depend upon a desired political outcome.
1.7.7.1. Pro: Palestine is a legitimate state and deserves to be recognised as such.
1.7.7.1.1. Con: Palestine is not a sovereign state in accordance with the [traditional concept of Statehood](http://www.politicalsciencenotes.com/essay/sovereignty-meaning-and-characteristics-of-sovereignty/254).
1.7.7.1.1.1. Pro: Palestine [does not have contiguous borders](http://america.aljazeera.com/multimedia/2014/7/west-bank-security.html), but is instead made up of an archipelago of areas of control, broken up by Israeli settlements and highways.
1.7.7.1.1.1.1. Con: It is unclear why the nature of a state's borders bears on its legitimacy, particularly in a modern context in which physical travel is less important.
1.7.7.1.1.1.2. Con: Other countries, too, have split territories and exclaves. French Guiana is part of France, Alaska part of the United States and Kaliningrad Oblast part of Russia, even though none of them share a border with their country's main territory.
1.7.7.1.1.1.3. Con: It is circular to deny Palestine the recognition of a state, which would presumably consolidate its territory, because its territory is not consolidated at the moment.
1.7.7.1.1.2. Con: The legal definition of a state, as enshrined in international law, is outlined in the [Montevideo Convention of Statehood](https://www.ilsa.org/jessup/jessup15/Montevideo%20Convention.pdf). Palestine fulfils this criteria .
1.7.7.1.1.2.1. Pro: Palestine has the "capacity to enter into relations with the other states" as it has a web of [diplomatic representations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Palestine) around the world.
1.7.7.1.1.2.2. Pro: Palestine clearly fulfills the [territory](https://www.google.de/maps/place/Palestine/\@31.9198698,34.6425902,9z/data=!4m5!3m4!1s0x151cf2d28866bdd9:0xee17a001d166f686!8m2!3d31.952162!4d35.233154) criteria as it rests upon a strip on the West Bank and in Gaza.
1.7.7.1.1.2.3. Pro: Palestine has a permanent population of around [4.7 million](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Palestinian_territories). Therefore Palestine fulfils criteria 1\(a\) of the Montevideo Convention.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4. Con: Palestine lacks a single sovereign government which can enforce laws throughout its dominion.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.1. Con: Official recognition of statehood by the US could facilitate processes to unify control of Palestine; the granting of statehood could be made contingent on this happening.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.1.1. Pro: Fatah and Hamas have [already indicated](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/1.765719) a willingness to form a unity government. US recognition could enable greater international cooperation in the formation of that government.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.2. Con: Even though Abbas's government does not have control over the entire territory, it is already the only sovereign recognized by most world governments, including the United Nations, whose [representative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations) is appointed by Abbas. In this respect, it is no different than any other state that does not fully control its territory.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.3. Con: [Pakistan](http://foreignpolicy.com/2014/08/26/militancy-in-pakistan/), [Nigeria](http://studies.aljazeera.net/en/reports/2016/06/resurgence-militancy-nigerias-oil-rich-niger-delta-dangers-militarisation-160608065729726.html), [India](http://www.thestatesman.com/opinion/islamic-militancy-in-india-1478730250.html), [Ukraine](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/interactive/2017/02/ukraine-map-170205081953296.html), and [Phillippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_in_the_Philippines) are just a few of the many states in the world that have militant organisations carrying out violent atrocities within their borders, yet they are all recognised as states.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.3.1. Con: As it is more difficult to revoke recognition than to initially grant it, the examples are different from Palestine.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.4. Pro: Palestine is [politically divided](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/markaz/2015/09/21/hamas-or-the-palestinian-authority-who-will-fail-first/) between two factions: Hamas, which controls the Gaza Strip, and Fatah which controls the West Bank.
1.7.7.1.1.2.4.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.5.
1.7.7.1.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.7.7.1.1.2.4.
1.7.7.1.1.4. Pro: Palestine does not have a [monopoly on violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopoly_on_violence) over the area it claims.
1.7.7.1.1.4.1. Pro: Israeli forces [regularly conduct raids](http://english.wafa.ps/page.aspx?id=6kwWfka60076552866a6kwWfk) into Palestinian areas of the West Bank to arrest suspected terrorists.
1.7.7.1.1.4.1.1. Con: Israeli intrusion should not render a state illegitimate: the US frequently intervenes militarily in countries without their consent, but that does not make their governments illegitimate.
1.7.7.1.1.4.1.2. Con: The frequency of these raids would presumably diminish drastically if this recognition strengthened the ability of the Palestinian state to maintain control itself.
1.7.7.1.1.4.2. Con: Recognition of statehood from the US could increase the ability of Palestinian governments to exert power within their borders and establish a monopoly on violence.
1.7.7.1.1.4.3. Con: -> See 1.7.7.1.1.2.4.3.
1.7.7.1.1.4.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.2.2.1.1.1.9.1.1.
1.7.7.1.2. Con: Palestinians have a [right to a nationality](http://www.ohchr.org/EN/Issues/Pages/Nationality.aspx) \(to be citizens of a country\), however this does not imply a UN right to have a state of their own. Their rights to security and a stable life could equally be satisfied by giving them citizenship in another country \(for example Israel or Jordan\).
1.7.7.1.2.1. Pro: [Millions of Palestinians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinians_in_Jordan) already have, or are eligible to apply for, Jordanian citizenship. This indicates that Palestinians can be provided with citizenship in either Jordan, or other states.
1.7.7.1.2.1.1. Con: Jordan has recently been [arbitrarily withdrawing citizenship](https://www.hrw.org/report/2010/02/01/stateless-again/palestinian-origin-jordanians-deprived-their-nationality) from people of Palestinian origin.
1.7.7.1.2.1.2. Con: Jordan has [no](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/4615/jordan-palestinians) interest in accepting Palestinians as its own citizens, not least because it fears being transformed into a Palestinian state. It currently refuses entry to, or forcibly deports, Palestinian refugees.
1.7.7.1.2.2. Pro: The Rohingya are a stateless group within Myanmar, however, the [UN calls for Myanmar to give them citizenship](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/americas/2014/12/un-calls-full-rohingya-citizenship-myanmar-monks-rakhin-2014123044246726211.html), and rejects giving them a state of their own, despite [some Rohingya groups](http://cartogracy.com/conflict/rohingya) fighting for independence.
1.7.7.1.2.2.1. Con: This approach has not been particularly effective in protecting the Rohingya, who many observers believe face [genocide](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/asia/rohingya-muslims-burma-government-rapes-massacres-government-genocide-ethnic-cleansing-rakhine-a7471636.html). There is no reason to believe it would be any more effective in helping the Palestinians either.
1.7.7.1.2.3. Con: -> See 1.7.7.1.2.1.2.
1.7.7.1.2.4. Con: -> See 1.1.2.5.5.
1.7.7.1.2.5. Pro: Many Palestinians are [eligible for Israeli citizenship](http://www.timesofisrael.com/more-east-jerusalem-palestinians-seek-israeli-citizenship/), yet they remain stateless for ideological reasons.
1.7.7.1.2.5.1. Con: This applies [only](http://articles.latimes.com/2014/jan/14/opinion/la-oe-myers-israel-citizenship-arabs-20140114) to Palestinians living in East Jerusalem, not the millions living in the rest of the occupied territories.
1.7.7.1.2.5.2. Con: Offering Palestinians Israeli citizenship as their only option coerces them into accepting citizenship in a nation that has repeatedly committed atrocities against their people. This is reprehensible.
1.7.7.1.3. Con: -> See 1.2.
1.7.7.1.4. Pro: Palestinians have a right to self-determination because they lived on the land in question for a longer period of time than the Israelis.
1.7.7.1.4.1. Con: It was not the fact of owning land, but the [British Mandate for Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Mandate_for_Palestine_\(legal_instrument\)#Establishment_of_a_national_home_for_the_Jewish_people) that established the mechanism for Israeli statehood.
1.7.7.1.4.1.1. Con: The British Mandate for Palestine was a piece of legislation produced by a colonial organisation, the League of Nations, with little regard for the rights of Palestinian Arabs. It should not be considered a legitimate cession of Palestinian moral ownership of the area.
1.7.7.1.4.1.1.1. Con: There was no sovereign entity in history named Palestine until the Mandate for Palestine. Indeed the Arabs who inhabited the land at the time saw themselves as Arabs or Syrians. The mandate was a legally binding instrument created by the League of Nations and backed by the San Remo declaration and the treaty of Sevres \(1920\) whereby the previous sovereign- Ottoman Turkey- divested itself of any claims to the area. The mandate recognised the rights of Jews to reconstitute their national home.
1.7.7.1.4.2. Pro: Expulsions and the illegal occupation of land that had been temporarily vacated during the war of 1948, called [the Palestinian Exodus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus), shaped the land claim of the early Israeli state.
1.7.7.1.4.3. Pro: Because Palestinians were forcibly expelled from Israel, their claim to sovereignty over the area was never legitimately extinguished, so they still enjoy a right to sovereign control over parts of the Israel/Palestine area.
1.7.7.1.4.3.1. Con: Palestinians never had a claim to sovereignty over the area in the first place; [Britain did](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandatory_Palestine), as Palestine prior to 1948 was part of the British Mandate.
1.7.7.1.4.4. Con: -> See 1.2.6.1.
1.7.7.1.4.5. Pro: Palestinians inhabited an even greater area than now but much of their land was [stolen](http://www.slate.com/articles/news_and_politics/the_gist/1997/05/selling_land_to_jews.html) by Israel.
1.7.7.1.4.5.1. Con: While individual Palestinians may have claims to land because it was stolen from them, this doesn't establish the legitimacy of a Palestinian state that postdates this theft.
1.7.7.1.4.5.1.1. Con: All Palestinians have suffered from the flow-on consequences of the initial theft of land; they therefore all have a moral claim to the land.
1.7.7.1.4.5.1.2. Con: At the very least, by indicating that the Israeli claim to the land is based on theft and therefore not legitimate, it strengthens the Palestinian claim to the land and therefore to self-determination.
1.7.7.1.4.5.1.3. Con: If modern Israel's legitimacy postdates its historical-right narrative, which is over 2,000 years old, then the 100 year-old right of Palestinians is also valid.
1.7.7.1.4.5.2. Con: This ignores the fact that Jews in British mandated Palestine existed and can be considered 'Israeli', and that a vast amount of modern day Israel was [legally purchased](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_land_purchase_in_Palestine) off Arab inhabitants. The land wasn't considered 'stolen' when it was under Jordanian control and Egyptian control.
1.7.7.1.4.5.2.1. Con: As of 1945, only around 7% of Historic Palestine was Jewish-owned. It is hard to imagine how the remainder - almost 19.000 square km - could have been legally purchased off Arab inhabitants.
1.7.7.1.4.5.2.1.1. Pro: In 1945, organizations such as the JNF and PICA owned [906.80 sq km](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_land_purchase_in_Palestine#Land_purchases), which was half the Jewish-owned land in the region. Twice that - all the land in Jewish hands - made up merely 7% of the the combined area of [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Israel), the [West Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank) and [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip).
1.7.7.1.4.5.3. Con: The land could not be stolen by a state that did not yet exist. If the land was stolen then it was stolen by someone else \(e.g. the British\).
1.7.7.1.5. Pro: The decision to recognize or not recognize the legitimacy of the Palestinian state is an important way in which other states signal their stance on the Israel/Palestine conflict, irrespective of any theoretical set of criteria for statehood. Acknowledging its legitimacy is thus a way of acknowledging the legitimacy of the Palestinian side of the conflict.
1.7.7.1.6. Pro: Recognition by many other nations is a sufficient condition for a state to be legitimate.
1.7.7.1.6.1. Pro: Political legitimacy is a social construct, and the political legitimacy of a state's existence depends solely on the number of other states willing to recognise that state's existence.
1.7.7.1.6.2. Pro: Many other states have recognised, or indicated their willingness to recognise, an independent Palestinian state.
1.7.7.1.6.2.1. Pro: Palestine has [more states recognising it](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition) than any other partially-recognised state not recognised by the US.
1.7.7.1.6.2.2. Con: Several other polities are partially recognised, however the US has not historically seen this as a compelling reason to recognise them itself.
1.7.7.1.6.2.2.1. Pro: 84 UN states [recognise the Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic) \(Western Sahara\), however the US does not.
1.7.7.1.6.2.2.2. Pro: The Republic of China \(Taiwan\) is [recognised by 19 UN member states as well as the Vatican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Taiwan#Entities_with_full_diplomatic_relations_with_Taiwan), but not by the US.
1.7.7.1.6.2.2.3. Con: Many other non- or partially-recognized polities are of little relevance for the United States. But in the case of Palestine, and as pointed out elsewhere in this debate, recognition would come with numerous benefits for America and its interests.
1.7.7.1.6.2.2.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.
1.7.7.1.6.2.3. Pro: The European Union has consistently declared its support and readiness for recognising a Palestinian state. This is outlined in both the [1980 Venice Declaration](http://eeas.europa.eu/archives/docs/mepp/docs/venice_declaration_1980_en.pdf) and [Berlin Declaration of March 1999](http://www.jcpa.org/jl/vp418.htm).
1.7.7.1.6.2.3.1. Con: This rhetorical commitment is not particularly significant. More than half of the EU's members and its five largest countries do not recognize Palestine as a state - a step they could easily take without incurring any significant cost.
1.7.7.1.6.2.3.2. Pro: The EU has [invested significantly](http://www.ecfr.eu/article/commentary_five_reasons_to_recognise_a_palestinian_state360) in the two-state solution, with almost €2.5 billion given by EU member states in support of Palestinian state building efforts since 2007. This is in addition to an annual contribution of over €200 million towards UNRWA, the Relief Work Agency that carries out work in the occupied territories.
1.7.7.1.6.2.4. Pro: 135 members of the UN [recognise](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2014/11/07/map-the-countries-that-recognize-palestine-as-a-state/?utm_term=.75a6e0dbe01e) Palestine as a state. Palestine was therefore recognised by a [higher percentage of nations](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/dashanne-stokes/is-this-the-real-reason-why-us-wont-recognize-palestine_b_9777246.html) at the time of its failed application to the U.N. in 2011 \(68 percent\) than Israel was \(64 percent\) when it was successfully admitted in 1949.
1.7.7.1.6.2.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.2.1.2.
1.7.7.1.7. Pro: The conquest of Palestinian territories by Israel in the [Six-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War) was illegitimate.
1.7.7.1.7.1. Con: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.11.
1.7.7.1.7.2. Con: As the land taken in the defensive war did not belong to any entity called "Palestine" framing the claim as a "conquest of Palestinian territories" is fallacious. The area in question had been held by Jordan.
1.7.7.1.8. Con: The current nonexistence of a Palestinian state is [due to](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_Palestine) the rejection of a partition plan by Arab leaders in 1948 and subsequent acts of warfare against the new state of Israel by Arab nations. Given that Palestinians voluntarily forfeited their opportunity to receive a state, they are not entitled to one now.
1.7.7.1.8.1. Con: The actions of historical leaders from other nations are irrelevant when it comes to considering the rights of modern-day Palestinians.
1.7.7.1.8.1.1. Con: If the actions of historical leaders from other nations are irrelevant, then the actions of current leaders from other nations are irrelevant. The passage of time wouldn’t do anything to make leaders from other nations more relevant. Therefore, the United States and other nations shouldn’t get involved in the rights of modern-day Palestinians.
1.7.7.1.8.2. Con: The U.N. partition [recommendation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine) called for more than half of then Palestinian land to be allocated for a “Jewish State”. This was unreasonable as the Arabs were a majority in Palestine at the time, and owned more land than Jews in every single district in the region. The 1948 plan was unfair and deserved to be rejected.
1.7.7.1.8.2.1. Con: Even if the agreement was unfair, the violent reaction against Israel from surrounding Arab nations was unjustified.
1.7.7.1.8.2.1.1. Con: We would not say, "Even if the occupation of Poland was unfair the violent reaction against Germany was unjustified."
1.7.7.1.8.3. Pro: The actions of historical and modern leaders from other nations are relevant when it comes to considering the rights of modern day Palestinians.
1.7.7.1.8.4. Pro: Palestine as a country never existed until the mid to late 20th Century. Palestine is a region of the Middle East that Israel, parts of modern day Jordan, Syria, and Lebanon exist in.
1.7.7.1.8.4.1. Pro: Arab leaders in 1919 denied that there is an entity called Palestine. To make claims about any native or pre-existing Palestinian identity therefore does not make sense and flies in the face of historical claims made by the Arabs themselves \([Bard, p. 3](https://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/jsource/images/mf2017.pdf#page=10)\).
1.7.7.1.9. Pro: The people of Palestine have the right to self-determination. Recognizing their state would also recognize this right.
1.7.7.1.9.1. Pro: The Palestinian people have the right to self-determination on the basis of how long they have lived on the land.
1.7.7.1.9.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.6.
1.7.7.1.9.1.2. Con: -> See 1.2.
1.7.7.1.9.1.3. Con: This is an arbitrary way of deciding which people have a right to the land, as there is no set period after which these rights come into being.
1.7.7.1.9.2. Pro: The Palestinians have a [right to self-determination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination) and to chose their political status on the basis that they are a people.
1.7.7.1.9.2.1. Con: Even if the Palestinians are recognized as a people, the way they want to self-determine can hardly be gauged due to the lack of a unitary government.
1.7.7.1.9.2.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.7.7.1.1.2.4.4.
1.7.7.1.9.2.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.5.5.4.2.
1.7.7.1.9.2.2. Con: It is [not clear](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-determination#Defining_"peoples") how to define "peoples" and whether the Palestinians therefore have the right to self-determination.
1.7.7.1.9.2.2.1. Pro: In numerous cases the applicability of the right to self-determination is disputed, for example in the case of the [Kurdish people](http://opiniojuris.org/2017/09/28/kurds-right-self-determination-andor-secession/) and the [Basque people](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-spain-basque-self-determination/spains-basque-country-proclaims-right-to-self-determination-idUSKBN0E91R720140529).
1.7.7.1.9.2.3. Con: No, they don't. They are Arabs, mostly Jordanian or Syrian, not any distinct people. They have no distinct history or culture. They never had their own nation at any time in history. The name Palestinian was pushed in the 1960's for the express purpose of sounding like one and arguing for a country.
1.7.7.1.9.2.3.1. Con: It shouldn't matter how far the history of a people goes back. The Palestinians of today have a distinct history and culture, for example on their basis for recognition and self-determination.
1.7.7.1.9.2.3.2. Con: By the same logic, the people of Israel should not have the right to self-determination and a state of their own. Israel was founded in 1948, after all.
1.7.7.1.9.3. Con: If the right of the Palestinian people to self-determination clashes with the same right of the Jewish people, it is not clear how both can be respected.
1.7.7.1.9.4. Con: The right to self-determination is [not a tangible element](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law:epil/9780199231690/law-9780199231690-e873) of international law and has no clear content or obligations; it is rather a vague moral principle recognized by various bodies.
1.7.7.1.9.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.7.7.1.9.2.2.
1.7.7.1.9.4.2. Pro: Even where there is agreement on the existence of a people, it is [not clear](http://opil.ouplaw.com/view/10.1093/law:epil/9780199231690/law-9780199231690-e873) what the right to self-determination entails and how precisely it can be exercised.
1.7.7.1.9.5. Pro: In 1988, Jordanian kingdom made an unconstitutional agreement with Israel regarding CisJordanian people who lost their nationality and Israel never considered them as Israeli people. Stateless, they chose to become Palestinians, as a nationality. These people exist. Therefore, Palestine is their State.
[journals.openedition.org](https://journals.openedition.org/ema/1745)
1.7.7.1.10. Con: -> See 1.1.1.5.
1.8. Pro: -> See 1.7.7.1.
1.9. Con: -> See 1.1.4.
1.10. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.13.4.1.
1.11. Con: Part of Palestine, the Gaza Strip, is ruled by [Hamas](https://www.nytimes.com/2014/10/10/world/middleeast/palestinians-gaza-cabinet-hamas.html), a group that the US recognises as a radical Islamist terrorist group. Recognising a Palestine that is partially ruled by Hamas is equivalent to legitimising a terrorist organisation.
1.11.1. Con: Hezbollah [exerts massive amounts of control](http://www.newsweek.com/hezbollahs-latest-conquest-lebanons-cabinet-541487) over Lebanon, however, the US still recognizes Lebanon's statehood.
1.11.1.1. Con: US recognition of Lebanon predates the creation of Hezbollah in [1982](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah).
1.11.1.2. Pro: Hezbollah is designated a [Foreign Terror Organisation](https://www.state.gov/j/ct/rls/other/des/123085.htm) by the US.
1.11.1.3. Con: Whereas Hamas controls the Gaza Strip, the influence of Hezbollah is smaller in day-to-day affairs. It holds [merely 9%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_general_election,_2017) of the seats in parliament, provides only [two out of 30](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_government_of_December_2016) ministers and neither the Prime Minister nor President.

1.13.11. Con: Palestinians have strong incentives not to recognise Israel as a Jewish state, and therefore should not do so.

[Protocol Additional to the Geneva Conventions of 12 August 1949, and relating to the Protection of Victims of International Armed Conflicts \(Protocol I\), 8 June 1977.](https://ihl-databases.icrc.org/applic/ihl/ihl.nsf/b0d5f4c1f4b8102041256739003e6366/6c86520d7efad527c12563cd0051d63c)

1.13.11.3. Pro: Accepting the Jewishness of the state would mean giving up the '[right of return](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_right_of_return)' for millions of Palestinian refugees into Israel who left during the 1948 exodus following the creation of Israel.
1.13.11.3.1. Con: There are not millions who left; there are less than 100,000 remaining. The "official" refugee community numbers in the millions only because the surrounding Arab states refuse to grant citizenship to the millions of children and grandchildren born within their borders.
1.13.11.3.2. Pro: Up to [8 million](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/4184/palestinian-refugees-return) Palestinian refugees wish to return to Israel, and strongly condemned Mahmoud Abbas's suggestion of giving up their right to return.
1.13.11.3.3. Pro: If this right to return is given up, up to 450,000 Palestinian refugees would be [forced](https://www.gatestoneinstitute.org/3770/lebanon-apartheid-laws) to continue to live in inhumane conditions in Lebanese refugee camps where they are treated as second-class citizens.
1.13.11.3.4. Con: Palestinian refugees do not have a right of return to Israel.
1.13.11.3.4.1. Pro: [Jewish leadership](http://www.slate.com/articles/news_and_politics/foreigners/2011/11/israel_and_1948_did_israel_plan_to_expel_its_arabs_in_1948_or_not_.html) did not plan to expel Arabs from the state-to-be of Israel; rather, that was the consequence of outbreak of violence between Arabs and Jews. As a result, the state of Israel bears no responsibility for Palestinians refugees.
1.13.11.3.4.1.1. Con: [According to Ilan Pappé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Ethnic_Cleansing_of_Palestine), Israeli Historian, the 1948 Palestinian exodus resulted from a planned ethnic cleansing of Palestine that was implemented by the Zionist movement leaders, mainly David Ben-Gurion, through systematic expulsions of about 500 Palestinian villages, as well as terrorist attacks executed mainly by members of the Irgun and Haganah troops against the civilian population. He also refers to Plan Dalet and to the village files as a proof of the planned expulsions.
1.13.11.3.4.2. Con: Of course they have a right to return. The [UN ruled as such in 1978](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/805C731452035912852569D1005C1201) and enshrines this concept in [Resolution 149](https://www.unrwa.org/content/resolution-194).
1.13.11.3.4.3. Pro: The refugee crisis was caused by the Arab invasion of Israel in 1948. Not only does the responsibility of solving the crisis lie on the shoulders of the Arab states that caused it, many of the Palestinian Arabs who fled did so [voluntarily](https://www.adl.org/education/resources/glossary-terms/palestinian-refugees) to avoid the ongoing war or at the urging of Arab leaders who promised that all who left would return after a quick Arab victory over the new Jewish state.
1.13.11.3.5. Con: Over 850,000 Jews were [expelled](http://www.timesofisrael.com/jewish-refugees-from-arab-lands-seek-justice-at-united-nations/) from Arab countries between 1948-70. These refugees have not been given a right of return to their homelands by Arab states, so it is hypocritical to demand that just for Palestinian refugees.
1.13.11.3.6. Con: Even if a right to return for Palestinian refugees did exist, granting it would not only [destroy](https://www.adl.org/education/resources/glossary-terms/palestinian-refugees) the Jewish character of Israel but also endanger its national security.
1.13.11.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.10.1.6.1.2.
1.13.12. Pro: The US should only be willing to recognise Palestine as part of a reciprocal recognition of Israel as Jewish by Palestinians. Recognising Palestine unconditionally gives away a valuable bargaining tool the US has to bring Palestine to the negotiating table. Once a Palestinian state is recognised, the Palestinian Authority has little incentive to negotiate.
1.13.12.1. Con: With the international community finally on its side, it makes little sense for the Palestinian Authority to act belligerent and uncooperative, laying waste to the diplomatic goodwill shown by the US in recognising it as a state.
1.13.13. Con: The demand for recognition as a Jewish state is new and surfaced only recently at the Annapolis Conference of [2007](http://foreignpolicy.com/2011/05/25/should-the-palestinians-recognize-israel-as-a-jewish-state/).
1.13.13.1. Pro: The demand to recognize Israel as a Jewish state is a [delaying tactic](http://foreignpolicy.com/2011/05/25/should-the-palestinians-recognize-israel-as-a-jewish-state/) by Israel.
1.13.13.1.1. Pro: There is [evidence](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/.premium-1.569459) that it was invented by Netanyahu to stymie peace processes with the Palestinians.
1.13.13.2. Con: The demand for a Jewish state is as old as Zionism itself. The Zionist program, adopted at the [First Zionist Congress in Basel in 1897](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/first-zionist-congress-and-basel-program-1897), specified that the “aim of Zionism is to create for the Jewish people a home in Palestine, secured by public law.”
1.13.13.2.1. Pro: '[The Jewish State](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/quot-the-jewish-state-quot-theodor-herzl)', written by Theodor Herzl, is considered to be the foundational text of the Zionist movement and the creation of Israel.
1.13.13.3. Con: The [Balfour Declaration](http://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/the-balfour-declaration) \(1917\), the [League of Nations Mandate for Palestine](http://www.mythsandfacts.org/conflict/mandate_for_palestine/mandate_for_palestine.htm) \(1922\), the [Peel Commission Report](http://www.jewishvirtuallibrary.org/text-of-the-peel-commission-report) \(1937\), and the [General Assembly Partition Resolution](https://unispal.un.org/DPA/DPR/unispal.nsf/0/7F0AF2BD897689B785256C330061D253) \(1947\), all recognise a 'Jewish' homeland for the Jews of Israel.
1.13.13.4. Pro: The demand for recognition as a Jewish state was not included in the treaties with [Jordan](http://www.kinghussein.gov.jo/peacetreaty.html) or [Egypt](http://www.mfa.gov.eg/Lists/Treaties%20DB/Attachments/645/Peace%20Treaty_en.pdf).
1.13.13.5. Con: -> See 1.1.4.10.1.6.1.2.6.3.
1.13.14. Pro: The fact that Palestinians do not recognize Israel as a Jewish state is an obstacle to the peace process. The US should therefore demand Palestinian recognition of Israel as a Jewish state before recognizing Palestine.
1.13.14.1. Con: Recognition of Israel as a Jewish state would make Arab residents of Israel feel unwelcome and marginalized, leading to domestic problems that could impede a peace process.
1.13.14.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.10.1.6.1.2.
1.13.14.2. Con: -> See 1.1.4.9.
1.13.14.3. Pro: Recognising a Palestine which does not accept Israel as a Jewish state could be seen as a tacit support for anti-Semitism by the United States.
1.13.14.4. Pro: It is only once a Jewish state is recognised that the Jewish people will no longer feel threatened; otherwise opposition to a Jewish state will be seen as continuing opposition to Israel in practice \([Becker, p. 13](https://www.washingtoninstitute.org/uploads/Documents/pubs/PolicyFocus108.pdf)\).
1.13.14.4.1. Pro: Only when there is a feeling of security among Israelis can there be true reconciliation.
1.13.14.4.2. Pro: The acceptance of their state's right to exist is particularly important for the people of Israel as they saw themselves opposed by a coalition of states in the past that attacked them with the [explicit goal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War#The_Arab_League_as_a_whole) of erasing them from the map.
1.13.14.4.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.1.2.
1.13.14.4.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.3.1.4.6.1.3.3.1.9.1.3.3.1.1.
1.13.14.4.5. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.9.
1.13.14.5. Pro: Without guaranteeing the Jewish right to a homeland, it is difficult for Israel to engage in negotiations.
1.13.14.5.1. Con: The Jewish citizens of Israel already have a homeland, even though their state is not recognised as a Jewish one.
1.13.14.5.1.1. Con: -> See 1.13.14.4.
1.13.14.5.2. Con: -> See 1.13.13.
1.13.14.5.3. Con: This recognition is only required from the Palestinians, not the international community. There is no reason why Palestinian recognition of a Jewish state is what validates the existence of a Jewish homeland.
1.13.14.5.3.1. Pro: The Palestinian refusal to recognize Israel as a Jewish state is backed by the [Arab League](http://www.haaretz.com/middle-east-news/1.578785).
1.13.14.6. Con: -> See 1.13.13.1.
1.13.14.7. Con: If recognition of Israel as a Jewish state led to the expulsion of disloyal Arab-Israelis, it would create more problems for the peace process than it solves.
1.13.14.7.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.5.4.4.
1.13.14.7.2. Pro: Right wing foreign minister [Avigdor Lieberman](http://www.aljazeera.com/palestinepapers/2011/01/2011124105622779946.html) already plans to swap Arab-Israeli villages in Israel with Jewish-Israeli settlements in the West Bank.
1.13.15. Con: Not all Israelis demand the Palestinian recognition of Israel as a Jewish state.
1.13.15.1. Pro: Haredi Jews, who make up 10% of Israel's population, and are expected to make up 25% of the population within a few decades, are, oftentimes violently, [opposed](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/belief/2016/may/12/for-haredi-jews-secular-zionism-remains-a-religious-heresy) to the idea of a Jewish state.
1.13.15.2. Pro: Members of the political establishment disagree on whether formal recognition as a Jewish state should be demanded.
1.13.15.2.1. Pro: [Shimon Shamir](http://www.haaretz.com/ask-mustafa-khalil-1.282123), former ambassador to Egypt and Jordan, regards the Jewishness of Israel as an internal matter that should not be put in front of the international community.
1.13.15.2.2. Pro: [Yonatan Touval](http://www.nytimes.com/2009/05/13/opinion/13iht-edtouval.html), director of international affairs at Tel Aviv University, criticized the demand as an obstacle to peace and as a danger to Arab-Israelis.
1.13.15.3. Con: For half the Jews in Israel, the recognition of their state as the Jewish homeland by the Palestinians is far more important than a peace deal. Only a slim majority does not perceive these issues as important \([IDI, p. 6](http://www.peaceindex.org/files/Peace_Index_Data_April_2016-Eng\(1\).pdf)\).
1.13.16. Con: It is inappropriate to demand from Palestine the recognition of Israel's right to exist or of Israel as a Jewish state.
1.13.16.1. Pro: -> See 1.13.11.1.
1.13.16.2. Con: -> See 1.13.14.4.
1.13.16.3. Con: Recognition by many other nations is a sufficient condition for a state to be legitimate. Therefore, Palestine should recognize Israeli statehood.
1.13.16.4. Pro: Recognition by many other nations is a sufficient condition for a state to be legitimate. Therefore, Palestinian recognition of Israel has no positive effects on Israel, but strengthens Israel's position in relation to already occupied land, its general approach to the Palestinian people, and potential war crimes.
1.13.16.5. Con: Due to the security issues that arise from such close proximity to Israel, and in order to create a lasting climate devoid of hatred but filled with mutual understanding, the above is a crucial first step Palestinians must take before recognizing Palestine.
1.13.16.5.1. Pro: The modern history of European Jewry shapes the current Israeli position regarding their 'right to exist': security predicates peace. Hamas' repeated calls for the destruction of Israel is bound to jog Jewish memories of these tragic times and establish a powerful negative association by contagion.
1.13.16.6. Pro: -> See 1.13.5.
1.13.16.7. Con: Israel is a de jure state. Thus the Palestinian rejection thereof is equivalent to the Palestinians rejecting the sun. It is no more than an International Relations game, which given their dependency on Israel, is counter-productive.
1.13.16.8. Con: By refusing to recognize Israel's right to exist, Palestine positions itself in opposition to many of its international supporters. This is inappropriate and egregious as the Palestinian economy and society are [highly dependent](http://www.themedialine.org/featured/international-aid-lifeline-palestinian-economy/) on international support.
1.13.16.8.1. Pro: A Palestine that opposes Israel's right to exist puts Germany in a problematic position vis-à-vis its support for Palestine. In the word's of [Angela Merkel](https://knesset.gov.il/description/eng/doc/speech_merkel_2008_eng.pdf), her country has a "special historical responsibility for Israel's security" which "will never be open to negotiation".
1.13.16.8.2. Pro: Opposing Israel's right to exist complicates relations with the US. As Barack Obama [told](https://www.nytimes.com/2013/03/22/world/middleeast/transcript-of-obamas-speech-in-israel.html) the people of Israel that those "who adhere to the ideology of rejecting Israel’s right to exist -- they might as well reject the earth beneath them and the sky above". "You are not alone" as long as the US exists.
1.13.16.9. Pro: Other states have not recognised Israel as a Jewish state, or been asked to, yet the US does not refuse to recognise those states.
1.13.16.9.1. Con: Most other states are not proximate to Israel or heavily involved with Israel geopolitically, so whether they recognise Israel or not is mostly irrelevant. The same is not true for Palestine.
1.13.16.9.1.1. Pro: Because the future of Palestine is integrally tied to the future existence of Israel and Israel's population, it's particularly vital that Palestine recognizes Israel's right to exist. The same is not true for other countries.
1.13.16.9.2. Con: It would be difficult for the US to withdraw its recognition of established states. In contrast to that, it is easy to reject the recognition of a disputed state.
1.13.16.9.3. Pro: -> See 1.13.14.5.3.1.
1.13.16.9.4. Pro: -> See 1.13.13.4.
1.13.16.9.5. Pro: Several major American allies, such as Pakistan and Saudi Arabia, as well as states that receive large amounts of US support, such as Afghanistan and Iraq, [do not recognize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Israel) Israel in the first place.
1.13.16.9.6. Con: At the same time, most other states have never rejected the right of Israel to exist. The context of their relations with Israel is thus different.
1.13.16.9.6.1. Con: Iranian leaders have rejected Israel's right to exist [on numerous occasions](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2015/03/Iranian-View-of-Israel/387085/), going so far as to describe it as Iran's mission to erase Israel from the map.
1.13.16.10. Pro: Other countries do not require recognition by other states of their affiliation with a certain religion.
1.13.16.10.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.10.1.6.1.2.1.1.
1.13.16.10.2. Pro: Countries like [Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Yemen) have, for all practical purposes, only Muslim citizens yet do not call for their international recognition as Islamic.
1.13.16.10.3. Con: Iran is generally referred to as the "Islamic Republic of Iran", even in the list of [UN member states](https://www.un.org/en/member-states/).
1.13.16.10.4. Pro: A [variety of countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_references_to_God) associate themselves with a certain religion through their constitution, from Australia and Poland to Switzerland and Ireland, yet they usually do not call for international recognition of this association.
1.13.16.11. Pro: No state besides Israel ever demands the recognition of its [right to exist](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/americas/2014/03/israel-pm-demands-recognition-jewish-state-20143418424955968.html) as a precondition for diplomatic engagement.
1.13.16.11.1. Con: That is because other states do not have their right to exist challenged consistently, as is the case with Israel.
1.13.16.11.1.1. Con: The Republic of China - better known as Taiwan - is not recognized as a state by the [vast majority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Taiwan#Entities_with_no_representation_in_Taiwan) of other states and has its right to exist as a state [rejected by China](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-34729538) frequently. Yet Taiwan does not constantly demand recognition.
1.13.16.11.1.1.1. Con: The reason that Taiwan does not demand this recognition is that China [would not tolerate it](http://www.reuters.com/article/us-china-taiwan-idUSKCN0YH08R). If Taiwan was in a position of greater security, it would likely demand recognition until it got it.
1.13.17. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.10.1.6.
1.13.18. Pro: One of the two former Prime Ministers of the Palestinian National Authority, Ismail Haniyeh, has [pledged](http://www.timesofisrael.com/hamas-official-denies-group-could-recognize-israel/) that he will not recognise Israel.
1.13.18.1. Pro: Ismail Haniyeh has recently been [elected](http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/05/ismail-haniya-elected-political-chief-hamas-170506115834018.html) as the new leader of Hamas' political bureau, which illustrates that his view is in line with the official policy of Hamas as an organisation, and therefore the people who vote for it.
1.13.18.2. Con: Hamas officials have publicly [accepted](http://www.npr.org/sections/thetwo-way/2011/05/24/136403918/hamas-foreign-minister-we-accept-two-state-solution-with-67-borders) the creation of two states along the 1967 boundaries. It is often Israel's aggression that provokes harsh rhetoric from Hamas.
1.13.18.3. Con: Hamas [outlined](http://edition.cnn.com/2006/WORLD/meast/01/29/hamas.interview/) conditions for a truce with Israel before the 2006 elections in Gaza, indicating how it is willing to be pragmatic when it comes to electoral pressures, even if it does not ideologically accept Israel's 'right to exist'.
1.13.18.4. Con: The same article quotes the Hamas leader as saying 'The question of recognition is non-debatable as long as \[Israel\] occupies our land'. While Hamas has not recognised Israel now, that does not mean it won't if independent states are formed along the 1967 boundaries.
1.13.18.4.1. Con: The organisation has been [adamant](http://www.haaretz.com/israel-news/hamas-leader-in-gaza-vows-group-will-never-recognize-israel-1.330593) that it will never recognise Israel.
